The Ministry of Finance Drafts Important Content of the Amended Organization Law

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance has drafted amendments to the points that should be amended again in the organization law of the Ministry that was amended and passed by the Legislative Yuan two weeks ago, taking into account the needs of the facts, and submitted it to the Executive Yuan's regular meeting for approval. After it is submitted to the Central Political Committee for approval, it can be sent to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. It is heard that the Ministry of Finance has decided to request that the points that should be amended again are all to improve the administrative efficiency of the Ministry, and are no different from those previously amended by the Legislative Yuan. The important contents have been ascertained to be as follows: 1. The organization laws of the Customs and Salt Administration both stipulate that the various departments and bureaus should submit certain matters to the Minister of Finance for approval and implement them in the name of the Ministry of Finance. The main amendment is to change the relevant matters to be implemented by orders of the departments or bureaus, without restricting the issuance of ministerial orders in the organization law of the departments and bureaus. 2. The Ministry of Finance should set up specialized commissioners. 3. The Ministry of Finance itself has already set up a Chief Accountant, and the Salt Administration under its jurisdiction should be renamed Chief Accountant and must contact the Chief Accountant within the Ministry. French Memorandum on Reply to Germany Published; Suggests Dividing into Political and Economic Parts; Advocates Establishing Lasting Peace in Europe

(Paris) The government has recently published two accompanying memoranda, one is a reply to the memorandum submitted by Germany on March 31, refuting the reasons on which the country based its abolition of the Locarno Pact, and the other is a peace plan. The first memorandum has been sent to the other signatory countries of the Locarno Pact, namely the governments of the United Kingdom, Belgium, and Italy. The second memorandum has been sent to each of these countries, as well as to the League of Nations. (Havas Telegram, 8th)

(Paris) France has now published a reply to the memorandum presented by German leader Hitler on April 1 regarding a new European peace plan. What has been published is a 13-page memorandum, which is divided into 25 sections detailing France's proposed declaration. The political section contains a proposal to organize a European Committee, advocating that obligations already undertaken should not be changed within 25 years. It also suggests establishing an international army and large-scale disarmament. The economic section discusses monetary stability, credit expansion, and market control. The final provision is that any event must be carried out within the League of Nations organization. French Foreign Minister Flandin and Minister Without Portfolio Peng Gu will inform other countries' representatives attending the Locarno Pact signatory countries' conference in Geneva of their decision on Hitler's memorandum.

The main point of the preamble to the French memorandum is: "Peace must be comprehensive and lasting, peace must have equal rights, peace must have trust in all parties' honor and respect for promises, and peace must be based on international trade, replacing economic nationalism competition to achieve stability." The declaration contains 25 sections, two of which specifically address "no hegemony," stating that lasting peace cannot be achieved if dominated by the needs or ambitions of the people, and the security of international relations cannot be achieved if disputes are not resolved by impartial interpretation and binding international law. Mutual assistance must be stipulated by local treaties. It also states that treaties must not be considered immutable forever, but they must also not be unilaterally abandoned.

Under the title of political measures, the French reply declares that Europe is a local unit. If Europe is too large to apply mutual assistance and disarmament to collective security, then it may be possible to organize local agreements and local treaties regarding the independence of various countries, and various armaments restrictions should be placed under explicit mutual guarantees. Various sanctions, even the use of force when necessary, should be adopted to uphold international law. Countries within the scope of Europe should set up special armies, navies, and air forces, under the command of the League of Nations or the European Committee. The European Committee has permanent management rights over the implementation of treaties within its scope. In terms of disarmament, the extent of armament restrictions in each country should be decided by a two-thirds majority of the European Committee or other League of Nations organs. Each country has the right to appeal to the Supreme Permanent Arbitration Committee established by the League of Nations Administrative Council. The French reply also states that the demilitarization of the Rhineland is the only security guarantee for Europe. Germany does not want to be placed in the International Court of Justice at The Hague because it knows that its reasons will inevitably be rejected. Germany is unwilling to make the necessary gestures to contribute to the efforts of reconciliation with the other signatory countries of the Locarno Pact. Germany's peace plan is unfortunately only a contribution in name. What France wants to know is whether its proposed Western air treaty includes air force restrictions. Without restrictions, this is completely worthless. Germany's plan is completely insufficient to fix peacetime. Even if Germany rejoins the League of Nations today, it will inevitably withdraw from the League of Nations again if its demands for colonial rights cannot be satisfied. (Reuters Telegram, 8th)

First Memorandum

(Paris) France has published its memorandum in response to Germany's memorandum, known as the First Memorandum. Its content is divided into ten points, refuting one by one the reasons cited by Germany for abolishing the Locarno Pact. The main points are as follows:

(1) After the German government abolished the Locarno Pact on March 7 and sent troops into the Rhineland, the rule of law in Europe was undermined. To avoid international disputes, France did not take appropriate measures to immediately restore the original situation, but instead engaged in talks with the other signatory countries of the Locarno Pact, hoping to preserve the possibility of an amicable solution. The signatory countries of the Locarno Pact also considered Germany's dignity and presented a draft proposal on March 19. However, Germany considered it detrimental to its honor and failed to grant it equal rights, and therefore rejected it. In fact, no one had damaged Germany's honor, nor had anyone withheld equal rights. Furthermore, although Germany agreed to return to the League of Nations, it still demanded that the League of Nations Covenant be amended beforehand.

(2) The German memorandum discussed the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland from a historical perspective, stating that it conflicted with the Fourteen Points proposed by the late US President Wilson. In fact, when the Paris Peace Conference discussed the disarmament of the Rhineland in 1919, the German delegation never protested. The Locarno Pact was freely signed by Germany after the Allied forces withdrew from the Rhineland. Germany unilaterally abolished it, citing as its reason that the Treaty of Versailles was signed under duress, and that the Locarno Pact failed to revise the clauses in the Treaty of Versailles related to German territory. Therefore, Germany has the right to refuse to respect certain clauses in the Locarno Pact (namely, those concerning the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland). However, one cannot help but doubt the value of any treaty Germany might sign in the future, leading to the conclusion that Germany will raise issues regarding the current system of the Free City of Danzig and the autonomous region of Memel, demand revisions to the current borders of some European countries, and demand the return of its original colonies. Germany should clearly answer all these questions.

(3) Although Germany believes that the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact conflicts with the Locarno Pact, the other signatory countries of the Locarno Pact have not raised any objections. Germany's refusal to seek a ruling from the International Court of Justice in The Hague indicates that its reasons are insufficient.

(4) The signatory countries of the Locarno Pact are prepared to negotiate based on the proposals put forward in the German memorandum and to establish a new agreement to replace the Locarno Pact. However, these countries are unwilling to conduct any negotiations based on "faits accomplis." Moreover, after Germany abrogated the treaty, it repeatedly refused to compromise, resolutely rejecting both the withdrawal of some of the troops stationed in the Rhineland and the construction of defensive fortifications in the area. How can there be any possibility of conducting negotiations?

(5) Although the German memorandum has put forward various peace proposals, they can only be considered after Germany provides guarantees and is willing to fulfill its promises. "The demilitarized zone of the Rhineland is not only related to the security of France and Belgium, but also to the interests of all of Europe. After the abolition of this system, how should it be remedied? The German memorandum does not provide any promises." We believe that the extent to which Germany adheres to the principle of collective security can be seen in whether or not Germany builds defensive fortifications in the Rhineland.

(6) The proposed non-aggression pact in the German memorandum is far from complete. This pact plan fails to incorporate a collective security system and is also incompatible with the proposal to conclude mutual assistance pacts with Eastern European countries. In addition, Germany is a signatory to the Kellogg-Briand Pact and should not use war as an instrument of national policy. Even if a non-aggression pact is concluded in the future, how can it add to its original obligations? In short, France rejects any approach that divides Europe into eastern and western parts and only considers the security of Western Europe.

(7) France welcomes Germany's return to the League of Nations, but given its recent actions, the threat of a second withdrawal from the League cannot be prevented. As for Germany's proposal to establish an international arbitration court, it directly denies the authority of the International Court of Justice in The Hague and the Council of the League of Nations.

(8) The German proposal on disarmament does not contain quantitative or qualitative restrictions on land and air forces. While the issue of humanizing war is reasonable in itself, its effectiveness would be much greater if a mutual assistance system could be advocated to deal with future aggressor countries, so that war would not occur in the first place.

(9) France does not reject the proposal to promote relations between France and Germany, and will do its utmost to achieve this goal. The League of Nations is also attempting to achieve spiritual disarmament.

(10) France fulfills its international obligations at all times and does not need to amend its current constitution. On the contrary, maintaining peace must begin with mutual respect for rights and mutual cooperation in order to be effective. When disputes arise between countries, it is inappropriate to seek solutions independently with neighboring countries and disregard the principle of collective security.

"In short, the current state of European power politics must be recognized without reservation, and the status quo in Europe must be preserved through a system of mutual assistance. The German memorandum to the British government does not mention a single word about this." (Havas dispatch, August 8)

Second Memorandum

(Paris) In addition to submitting the First Memorandum to respond to the German memorandum, France also submitted a Second Memorandum, detailing a peace plan, stating first, "What the government of the French Republic is proposing now is to achieve universal, complete, and lasting peace by safeguarding the honor of all countries, fulfilling the promises of all countries, respecting the equal rights of all countries, and encouraging international trade, and to move from effectively limiting armaments to reducing armaments, in order to achieve true peace."

This plan is based on the following principles: equality of rights, respect for international obligations. The French government believes that peace cannot be expected if it is based on the needs and desires of various nations. International rule of law should have compulsory and adequate safeguards. Hegemony is not allowed. The French government believes that all countries may freely relinquish part of their sovereignty under certain circumstances, especially under the issue of armaments, and that universal mutual assistance pacts may be concluded to remedy any disparities in the military strength of various countries. (To be continued) (Havas dispatch, August 8)

Talks Between the Three-Nation General Staffs - Selection of British Representatives

Strong Opposition Sentiment in the Lower House Remains

(London) The British representatives to participate in the talks between the three-nation general staffs have been appointed: Major General Dill, Major General Amison, Colonel Ismay, Colonel Paget, and Sir Andam, totaling five persons, with Major General Dill as the chief representative. He is an outstanding talent among the younger British officers, having served as the principal of the General Staff College and an instructor at the Imperial Defence College. His knowledge and talent have always been highly respected in military circles. (Havas dispatch, August 7)

(London) Regarding the talks to be held between the British, French, and Belgian general staffs, Foreign Secretary Eden made an explanation to the House of Commons last Friday (the 3rd), stating that the measures that can be decided in these talks will only be effective during the period of general negotiations between the countries concerned. Their nature is purely technical, so politically it will not increase Britain's obligations, and the defence organizations of the countries concerned will not accept any constraints as a result. After this explanation, the atmosphere in the House of Commons seemed to have cleared up, and even those who most strongly opposed the principle of the talks seemed to have dispelled their doubts. Unexpectedly, when the House of Commons met this afternoon, opposition Labour MP Frychin and extreme Conservative MP Churchill successively raised questions to Prime Minister Baldwin on this issue, indicating that opposition sentiment towards these talks in some quarters of the House of Commons is now on the rise again. The following is a summary of the questions and answers between Frychin, Churchill, and Prime Minister Baldwin: Frychin asked, "Can the Cabinet provide assurance that the preparations for these talks are being made by the Cabinet and not the general staff?"

The Prime Minister replied, "The Cabinet has always closely monitored these talks. I have already told the members of the House of Commons this."

Frychin asked, "Can the Cabinet provide assurance that British military secrets will not be leaked?"

The Prime Minister replied, "The military officers of our country who are handling the affairs of the general staff talks are well known to me, and there will definitely be no leakage of secrets."

Churchill asked, "Regarding military secrets, is there a situation where one side leaks secrets and the other side does not?"

The Prime Minister replied, "What do you mean by 'secrets'? I really do not understand." (Havas dispatch, August 7)

Thirteen-Nation Committee Holds Secret Meeting to Discuss the Use of Poison Gas by Italian Troops - Britain and France Form an Opposing Stance

(Geneva) This morning, the Thirteen-Nation Committee held a closed-door meeting to discuss the Italian army's use of poison gas in Abyssinia. According to British Foreign Secretary Eden, the 1925 convention stipulated that the use of gas was absolutely prohibited, and both Italy and Abyssinia were signatories to the convention. French Foreign Minister Flandin called on both Italy and Abyssinia to begin peace talks, which have been going on for five weeks, but have not yet started. Is Italy prepared to start these talks? It is now time to know. The meeting was adjourned until 4:00 p.m. today. It is reported that League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol inquired with the Red Cross to see if the Red Cross could provide any evidence regarding the Italian army's use of poison gas in Abyssinia. (Reuters dispatch, August 8)

Thirteen-Nation Committee Holds Secret Meeting to Discuss the Use of Poison Gas by Italian Troops - Britain and France Form an Opposing Stance

(Geneva) When the Thirteen-Nation Committee met here today, British Foreign Secretary Eden questioned the committee as to whether it knew anything about Italy's use of poison gas. League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol replied that there was no evidence to show that this was true. Eden also said that the use of poison gas was prohibited by the 1925 Geneva Protocol, which Italy had signed, and should not have knowingly violated it. At this point, the French Foreign Minister stood up and demanded that the League of Nations investigate the Abyssinian army's use of dumdum bullets and the arbitrary killing of Italian prisoners. From this, it can be seen that the positions of Britain and France in Geneva have formed an opposing stance. The committee adjourned at 4:00 p.m. so that Spanish representative Madariaga and Avenol could inquire with the International Red Cross about this matter. The Mexican representative sent a letter from London to the League of Nations protesting against the League of Nations' delay in imposing sanctions on Italy, and stated that Mexico was unwilling to bear the responsibility for weakening collective peace. According to general observation, Britain's attitude towards Italy is becoming tougher again, while France's attitude towards Italy has changed again. (National Telegraph, August 8)

(London) According to well-informed sources who spoke to our correspondent, when the Thirteen-Nation Committee of the League of Nations Council meets in Geneva tomorrow, Foreign Secretary Eden will raise two demands: 1. An immediate investigation into the Italian army's methods of warfare in Abyssinia. 2. The Thirteen-Nation Committee should draft a basis for a peace plan so that a ceasefire can be achieved after the two warring countries accept the principles. However, if the committee's deliberations are unsuccessful, the League of Nations General Assembly's Eighteen-Nation Subcommittee should be convened immediately to tighten sanctions against Italy. The British government's intentions in making these demands are twofold: 1. To make Italy understand that delaying the matter is of no benefit to it. 2. To find ways to offset the advantages Italy has gained through military victories. It is generally known that the British government originally intended to demand the immediate convening of the Eighteen-Nation Subcommittee, but fearing that this move might force Italy to embrace Germany and conclude a military alliance with it, it abandoned its original plan. Political figures are generally pessimistic about the resolution of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, believing that if the peace efforts of the Thirteen-Nation Committee fail, Italy will inevitably choose between Germany and France. (Havas dispatch, August 7)

(Brussels) Prime Minister Janson is scheduled to take the train at 4:00 p.m. on Thursday, passing through Paris, to Geneva. The Thirteen-Nation Committee Meets - Abyssinia Issues Final Appeal to the League of Nations

Weakness Subjected to Aggression Endangers World Peace - Urgently Hopes for Effective Prevention

(Geneva) Abyssinian Foreign Minister Heruy has sent a telegram to League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol, issuing a final appeal to the League of Nations in the name of the Abyssinian government, stating, "The obligations stipulated in Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant are clearly stated, but the Italian government is still able to wage war against a weak and helpless nation with impunity. As for the methods of warfare used by the Italian army, which include bombing defenseless cities from the air and even using poisonous gas, they are truly brutal. At this moment, all the weak countries in the world believe that although the League of Nations Covenant has provisions for a collective security system, it is doubtful whether it can be relied upon, as the impact of the Italian-Abyssinian war has threatened all these small countries. "The invasion of Abyssinia by Italy puts world peace in danger, and the Abyssinian nation will be destroyed. It is hoped that the League of Nations will no longer stand idly by, but will quickly provide effective assistance to the invaded country, because the issue concerns not only the independence of Abyssinia." All Men in the Country Should Enlist - Italian Troops Take Advantage of Victory to Advance into Taysi

(London) According to a spokesman for the Abyssinian Embassy in Britain, the Abyssinian government has issued a general mobilization order, and all physically fit men in the country should enlist. In the future, the number of Abyssinian troops can be doubled compared to the current number. (Havas dispatch, August 7)

(Abyssinian Capital) This afternoon, the Abyssinian King's order to enlist all those who are able to serve in the military was read out in the palace. At the same time, observers on the northern front are asking each other, "Where is the Abyssinian King?" The Abyssinian King, fearing that he would be targeted by Italian bombers, abandoned his car and headed south on foot. His car has been captured by the Italian army. The Crown Prince is now leading 2,000 people north from Taysi to find and protect his father. It is reported that the armed bandits are killing Abyssinian King's defeated soldiers, which is quite cruel. The corpses are piled up along the way south of Guran, and the advancing Italian army must clear the roads with burial teams before they can move. The Crown Prince is afraid that his father will be in danger, so he has to go to protect him. The Italian army is currently advancing in two routes south of Guran, one along the "Imperial Road" to spy on Taysi, and the other towards Magdala. The Italian army now claims that the area of Abyssinian land that has fallen into the hands of the Italian army is as large as half of Britain. (Reuters dispatch, August 7)

(Rome) After occupying Guran, the Italian army on the northern front in East Africa, in addition to a part of the first column, is continuing to advance south to pursue the Abyssinian army. The rest of the troops are working hard to reorganize and clear the rear. A large number of workers have begun to rush to build the highway to Guran, so that the Italian army's tank and armored vehicle fleets can approach Taysi and threaten the Abyssinian army. According to the Italian military authorities, the date of launching the general offensive on Taysi is not far away. The Italian air force has been flying to Taysi to scout and bomb for days, which has been enough to make the remaining members of the Abyssinian Imperial Guard feel uneasy. (National Telegraph, August 7)

Unexpected Secondary Declaration - Respect for Egyptian Interests - Prepared to Conclude an Agreement - Maintaining the Status Quo of the Boundary

(Rome) The semi-official Stefani news agency recently published a statement made by Foreign Minister Suvich to the Egyptian Chargé d'Affaires, stating, "The claim that Italy intends to attack or threaten Egypt in some way is absurd. Italy has no intention of conquering Egypt as an Italian colony, and this is true now and will be true in the future. Strait of Tartary - Turkey Prepares to Restore Armaments

If Success Cannot Be Achieved Through Negotiations, the Treaty of Lausanne Will Automatically Be Declared Void

(Istanbul) According to news from Ankara, the Turkish capital, if the Turkish government cannot abolish the provisions in the Treaty of Lausanne regarding the demilitarization of the straits through negotiations, it may abolish it itself. It is reported that responsible parties in the country all believe that the rearmament of the Strait of Tartary is a matter of the utmost importance for Turkey's existence, as the general security situation in Europe has recently changed greatly, and both Germany and Austria have abolished the military clauses in the peace treaty. Although Turkey is keen to respect its commitments, it must do its utmost to achieve amendments regarding the fortification of the straits and Gallipoli. According to the Treaty of Lausanne, which was concluded in 1923, formally ended the state of war between Turkey and the Allied Powers, ceding East Thrace (including Adrianople) to Turkey, while Turkey abandoned its Palestinian and Iraqi territories to British trusteeship, abandoned Syria to French trusteeship, and abandoned the rest of Arabia. The most important clause in the treaty was the one regarding the straits. This clause guaranteed the freedom of the straits, and another special convention stipulated the demilitarization of the area on both sides of the Bosphorus Strait and the Sea of Marmara, and stipulated regulations to guarantee the freedom of the straits in times of peace and war, with a mixed commission sent by the League of Nations to monitor its implementation. (Reuters dispatch, August 7)

Spain President Forced to Resign

Due to illegal dissolution of Congress, Bariot was elected provisional president

Madrid: The "People's Front" (i.e., the left-wing Socialist Party, the Communist Party, and the Industrial Revolution Party) was indignant at President Zamora's interference in the work of Congress, and excited by its victory in the recent general election, and therefore proposed a motion to impeach the president, saying that Mr. Chai's dissolution of the Second Congress on January 7 was detrimental to the interests of the country. This motion was passed by a vote of 238 to 5, with both the left and right parties supporting it, and then the Speaker of the National Assembly, Bariot, the leader of the Radical Democratic Party, was elected provisional president. According to Mr. Chai's downfall, his end was revealed in January. At that time, the far-right parties and the "People's Front" opposed the cabinet formed by the former Liberal Party leader Valadares on December 14 and December 30. The first cabinet resigned eight hours after December 30 due to a dispute over the joint right-wing and central parties resisting the left wing in the general election. Mr. Valadares then formed a new government with a non-partisan faction. The new government decided not to hold a congressional meeting immediately and adjourned the meeting until January 31, so except for the non-partisan factions, they all opposed it, pointing out that it was close to arbitrary tactics, and tried to force Mr. Chai to convene Congress, and on the one hand, they planned to impeach Mr. Fa and his cabinet members. When the far-right parties were about to present the signatures of sufficient numbers of members to Congress, Mr. Fa took the lead and, with the permission of the president, ordered the dissolution of Congress. However, Mr. Fa's cabinet resigned on February 19 as a result of the "People's Front" winning a great victory in the general election, and the new government was formed by former Prime Minister Azaña to replace it. (Reuters telegram on the 8th)

Moscow Newspaper Comments on the Mutual Assistance Agreement Between Mongolia and Russia

(Moscow) The editorial of "Izvestia" stated that the draft mutual assistance signed in Kulun on March 12 is a clear example of unwavering efforts to strive for peace, and also an example of the Soviet Union's assistance to peaceful and friendly people on the basis of complete equality and mutual benefit, and their heroic struggle for their rights to survival and independence.

The people of the Soviet Union and the Mongolian People's Republic have been linked by close and unremitting friendship for fifteen years. This friendship arose in 1921 when they jointly resisted foreign enemies. At that time, the Soviet government accepted the request of the Mongolian People's Republic and sent the Red Army to Outer Mongolia to unite with the Mongolian People's Revolutionary Army to defeat the mercenary looting teams of Japanese interventionists. They wanted to enslave the Mongolian people and turn Outer Mongolia into a colony of Japan and a base for Japanese imperialism to continue to attack the Soviet Union. In this common victorious struggle, the mutual assistance agreement between the Soviet government and the government of the Mongolian People's Republic was born and realized, that is, in the future, when one of the contracting countries is threatened by a third party's military attack, it will still be effective. At the request of the government of Outer Mongolia, the Soviet government agreed to temporarily station a part of its troops in the territory of the Mongolian People's Republic in the same year until the danger of attack on the Mongolian People's Republic is eliminated. When the situation in the Far East made it unnecessary for Soviet troops to be stationed in Outer Mongolia, the Soviet government, with the consent of the government of the Mongolian People's Republic, withdrew all its troops from Outer Mongolia in early 1925.

When we reviewed the memorandum of the government of the Mongolian People's Republic on February 27, 1925, we thanked the Soviet government for its assistance to the Mongolian people as follows: "The government, on behalf of all the people of the Mongolian People's Republic, expresses its deep satisfaction and gratitude for the indelible friendship of the Red Army to the people of the Mongolian People's Republic. Please convey the deep gratitude of the Mongolian people to the workers and peasants of the Soviet Union and the heroic Red Army, the permanent protectors of the oppressed and enslaved people of the world, and the leading organs of your country.

The working people of the Mongolian People's Republic and its government all believe that the two countries will continue their sincere friendship and mutual assistance in times of common adversity in the future. Our people and government dare to believe deeply that if the situation of 1921 is ever seen again—which is not what we want—the Soviet Union and its Red Army will definitely provide assistance."

From this, we can see that even at the time of the signing of the Beijing Treaty in 1925, the Soviet Union and Outer Mongolia still maintained their deep friendship and mutual assistance relationship. This relationship was established in 1921 and is completely in line with the interests of China.

The great revolution of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, who devoted his life to the cause of the liberation of the Chinese people, fully confirmed that Soviet assistance was absolutely necessary to ensure the sanctity and integrity of Outer Mongolia and prevent it from becoming a base for attacking the Soviet Union and China. In the joint communiqué between Dr. Sun Yat-sen and the Soviet representative to China in January 1923, he pointed out that "the immediate withdrawal of Russian troops from Outer Mongolia is neither urgent nor in the real welfare of China. It will be due to the current Beijing government's inability to guarantee that after the withdrawal of Russian troops, the anti-Russian White Army will no longer carry out its conspiracies and create a more serious situation than it is now."

Soviet Union's guaranteeing the security of Outer Mongolia's border is not only a primary task for Soviet security, but also for China, and the Chinese government has the responsibility not to allow Outer Mongolia to become a base for attacking the Soviet Union, which was recorded in the Beijing Treaty. Article 5 of the treaty stated that the Soviet government recognizes Outer Mongolia as a component part of the Republic of China and respects China's sovereignty in the area. At the same time, the article stipulates that the Soviet Union's withdrawal of its troops from Outer Mongolia shall be carried out "the complete withdrawal of Soviet troops from Outer Mongolia and the meeting to discuss the date of withdrawal of troops and the means of ensuring border security shall be agreed upon."

This article has clearly indicated that the Chinese government has also recognized that the Soviet Union has the right to adopt various methods at a certain time, such as sending troops to the Mongolian People's Republic, to guarantee its border security. The method of withdrawing troops should have been discussed and agreed upon at the Sino-Soviet meeting according to the Beijing Agreement, which is very clear. However, this meeting has not been convened, which is not the fault of the Soviet Union but has been prevented by China's civil war and the instability of the Chinese government. However, the Soviet government, without waiting for the convening of the Sino-Soviet meeting, took the initiative and, with the consent of the government of the Mongolian People's Republic, immediately withdrew its troops when it was no longer necessary to station troops in the territory of the Mongolian People's Republic. At the same time, the Soviet government still has the obligation to assist the Mongolian people in maintaining the integrity and dignity of their territory, as well as economic and cultural construction. Therefore, in 1934, when the Mongolian People's Republic was again threatened by territorial invasion, the Premier of the Cabinet of the Mongolian People's Republic, Mr. Genden, proposed to the Soviet government that it request assistance when the Mongolian People's Republic was attacked. The two countries reiterated their obligation to provide each other with various mutual assistance—including military assistance—when they were attacked by a third country, which is only natural. This agreement was not formally signed, but was a verbal understanding, that is, the so-called gentleman's agreement.

When the Japanese-Manchu troops began to repeatedly attack the territory of the Mongolian People's Republic in 1935, the Soviet government repeatedly asked the Japanese government to pay attention to its deep concern for maintaining the dignity of Outer Mongolia. In fact, when the Japanese-Manchu army attempted to seize the territory of Outer Mongolia, it was difficult for the Soviet Union to stand by and watch. However, regardless of these stern repeated warnings, the attacks by the Japanese-Manchu army on the territory of the Mongolian People's Republic not only continued, but also took on a more provocative and bold nature. Therefore, in January 1935, the government of the Mongolian People's Republic believed that it was necessary to send a delegation to Moscow to formally revise the original verbal agreement into a public agreement on mutual assistance, allowing the Mongolian People's Republic to be given assistance. On January 25 this year, the Presidium of the "Small Khural" and the Cabinet meeting of the Mongolian People's Republic again requested assistance from the Soviet Union, and made a special written application, which was delivered to Kalinin and Molotov, and signed by the chairman of the "Small Khural", Mr. Amur, and the Premier of the Cabinet, Mr. Genden.

The Soviet government agreed to the request of the government of the Mongolian People's Republic and signed the draft agreement in Kulun on March 12, 1936, which more clearly stipulated the specific mutual assistance obligations. This obligation was established as early as 1921 on the basis of jointly resisting intervention. This agreement is also fully in line with the Beijing Agreement of 1924. The most unreasonable adventurers among the Japanese warlords are now trying to seize Outer Mongolia again. Obviously, the Soviet government's actions are fully in line with its various obligations to the Mongolian People's Republic and are for the maintenance of peace. This self-defense action will not infringe on the interests of the Chinese people in the slightest.

In the meeting between Howard and the leader of the Soviet people, Stalin, Mr. Shi declared in a frank and clear manner, "If Japan dares to attack the Mongolian People's Republic and attempts to infringe on its independence, then we have to assist the Mongolian People's Republic, just as we did in 1921." This statement has caused enthusiasm in the Soviet Union and the Mongolian People's Republic, and has received the greatest sympathy and understanding from all peace-loving friends in the world. The broad masses of the Chinese people have also seen from this statement the firm expression of the Soviet government's efforts to strive for peace, and know that the Soviet government's position is also in line with China's interests, because China is tired of resisting aggression and has no ability to guarantee the territorial security of the Mongolian People's Republic.

The March 12, 1936, draft agreement is a peaceful document, that is, even the worst enemy of the Soviet Union cannot obtain a word in the agreement except for warning those who invade the territory of other countries and that the Soviet Union is prepared to provide assistance when the Mongolian people become victims of aggression. The peace-loving Mongolian people have no plans for aggression or imperialism against their neighbors, and peace in the Far East is completely dependent on the neighbors, which is self-evident. (TASS Telegram on the 8th)

Hunan's New Cultural Movement: Promoting Innovation from the Foundation of Traditional Culture, Diligently Constructing Scientific Enterprises

Beijing Dispatch: Mr. Li Huarui, advisor to the Hunan Provincial Government and the First Route Army Headquarters for Bandit Suppression, recently made remarks in Beijing regarding Hunan's internal affairs, which aroused considerable interest from various parties. As Mr. Liu is about to return to Hunan, our reporter specially interviewed him again. Reporter: There are rumors that a "New Chinese Cultural Movement" will be launched in Hunan. Is this true? Mr. Liu: Launching a New Chinese Cultural Movement is Mr. He's sole objective in presiding over both military and civilian affairs in Hunan Province. Furthermore, this movement has already begun. If it continues for five to ten years, there will certainly be significant results. Reporter: Could you please provide examples of the New Chinese Cultural Movement projects? Mr. Liu: Hunan has achieved remarkable results in training in national martial arts. From elementary school, middle school, and university students to all counties and villages in the province, people are engaged in learning. We also promote traditional Chinese medicine, implement inherent moral education, advocate the study of classics, and operate various industrial and commercial enterprises. Reporter: Some people consider the items you mentioned as a step backward. How can they be considered a New Cultural Movement? Mr. Liu: There is a misunderstanding among the general public in China regarding this New Cultural Movement. It is considered a suicidal movement. Instead, it advocates negating the treasures of China's inherent civilization, the legacy of sages and scholars from the past five thousand years, deeming them worthless. This is a completely wrong path. For example, the scientific and civilized achievements of countries like England and the United States today did not come about by overthrowing all of England's old culture. When we examine the history of major industrial and civilized countries in the world, we find that their reformers and scientists all sought new discoveries based on the legacy of their ancestors. It certainly didn't arise from the English people refusing to speak English, write English characters, or read English books. The same is true for other countries. In the future, to generate genuinely new Chinese cultural enterprises, we must, on a large scale and thoroughly, promote innovation from the existing foundation. Reporter: Is there a concrete publicity plan for this movement? Mr. Liu: These kinds of enterprises require dedicated hard work and the cooperation of the entire nation. In the past, there was too much empty talk and superficial publicity. In the future, we must be faithful and exert our efforts. Reporter: What is the outline for this dedicated hard work? Mr. Liu: He Jian's governance, both politically and militarily, has culture as its objective. That is, both politics and military affairs should be directed by culture. Officials should not harm the people, and soldiers should not disturb the people. Everyone should engage in cultural construction for the country and their locality, using the power of politics and the military to develop and protect the dignity of five thousand years of national culture, and to cooperate with the world's new civilization. Reporter: According to you, Hunan is very energetic. However, there are still outsiders who speak ill of Hunan, and some publications even criticize Chairman He. Mr. Liu: It's hard to avoid praise and criticism. Even Confucius, George Washington, and Napoleon are still being criticized in books and articles. In short, He Jian and the future of Hunan will be evident to both domestic and international observers through facts. Reporter: What about Hunan's scientific enterprises? Mr. Liu: Hunan's cultural politics, industry, and commerce all possess a scientific spirit. The provincial government publishes the Hunan Yearbook, which provides a clear overview. The province has established an Industrial Experiment Institute, an Agricultural Experiment Institute, a Geological Survey Institute, a Social and Economic Survey Institute, and a Mineral Testing Institute. All of these have systematic scientific publications and remarkable achievements. They are all being carried out using scientific methods.

Miscellaneous Notes on Rural Hubei

(Special Correspondent of This Newspaper: Cheng Jun)

(4) Bandit Troubles and Local Conditions in Chongyang

The county has the Juan River, which was likely called Xiajuan in ancient times, hence the name. The river originates in Tongcheng County, traverses the county, flows down to Puji and connects to Hankou. It is the most beneficial river for the county, irrigating the fields on both sides, allowing for three harvests each year, without fear of flooding. In other areas, people value weirs more than ponds. The largest weirs are Huabei and Shizui. Because the four borders are mostly mountainous, there is no fear of water scarcity. The main agricultural products are rice, wheat, beans, potatoes, buckwheat, and five types of grains. In addition, tea, paper, and tung oil are also major products. However, the people are exceptionally lazy, especially the men. The cultivation of the fields mostly relies on women. The men are mostly idle, not only not diligently farming but also wasteful in their consumption, addicted to smoking and gambling. From Zhao Liqiao to Zongshi, the reporter traveled seventy li, and saw no more than one or two dozen farmers in the fields. The fields left uncultivated were no less than seven or eight out of ten. Initially, I thought it was not yet farming season or affected by the Red Bandits. Unexpectedly, the laziness was so extreme. On the 23rd, investigations near the county seat revealed that many farmers were as thin as firewood, all due to opium addiction. Therefore, even though the land is fertile, the farmers are still extremely poor. In good years, they have no savings, and in bad years, they inevitably face death. Among the entire county, the first and fourth districts are blessed by nature, and the people's nature is also unique. The second district is next. The third and fifth districts are the worst, but the farmers are relatively diligent. It can be seen that the blessings Heaven bestows upon the people of Chongyang are actually harming them. Last year, the third district suffered a severe drought. Chief Commander Chen Jicheng requested and obtained 11,000 yuan in disaster relief funds, which County Magistrate Gong Nan used to purchase grain, personally going to the villages to distribute it, saving many lives. Soon after, the price of tung oil increased tenfold. People collected tung oil in the mountains, each earning dozens of dan, reaping great profits. The tea, tung, bamboo, and other products of the mountains do not require human labor or fertilizer, naturally forming forests. The people of Chongyang only need to enjoy their benefits. The tea is black tea, traditionally sold to Russia. Now, very few Russians come to buy it, greatly affecting people's livelihoods. Bamboo can be made into paper, but people adhere to old methods and have not been able to improve it, so sales are not very smooth. In the entire county, owner-farmers and tenant-farmers each account for half. In the past, there were quite a few large landlords, but they have all moved elsewhere to avoid bandits. Hired farmers are divided into long-term laborers and short-term laborers. Long-term laborers are paid by the month, with wages of three yuan. Short-term laborers are paid by the day, with wages of one jiao five fen to two jiao. Those who provide their own food receive three jiao to four jiao.

As for the people's burden, in the past, taxes were divided into four types: land tax, rice tax, stored military rice tax, and eliminated military rice tax. Land tax was one yuan four jiao for every tael of silver for the basic tax, one jiao eight fen seven li for the provincial surtax, six yuan two jiao for local defense donation, five jiao six fen for county administration donation, and three jiao seven fen four li for education donation. Rice tax was two yuan eight jiao for the basic tax per dan, one yuan one jiao two fen for county administration donation, and two jiao six fen two li for education donation. Stored military rice tax was one yuan four jiao nine fen four li for the basic tax per dan, and three yuan six jiao for the local defense donation. Eliminated military rice tax was one yuan three jiao seven li for the basic tax per dan, and three yuan six jiao for the local defense donation. Stored military rice tax and eliminated military rice tax were special taxes left over from the Qing Dynasty. Last winter, the dan-tael system was abolished and replaced with the mu (acre) system for collecting national currency. The total area in the county is 250,015 mu, with a basic tax of one jiao four fen per mu, a mu donation of two jiao eight fen, an additional five fen for county administration donation, and two fen for education donation. Each year, it is collected in two installments, during the spring and autumn harvests. The people complain that the mu donation is too heavy and they cannot afford it. Regarding excessive and miscellaneous taxes, before the 20th year of the Republic [1931], the Baiyuntan Township in the county had a production tax collection office, collecting taxes on rice, grain, leather, oil, firecrackers, and paper. With the representation of fellow villagers in the provincial capital, such as Pang Buqi, it was approved for abolition. Although a few taxes remain, they are close to being excessive and miscellaneous, but they are collected voluntarily by the people to support schools, so generally there is no significant problem. Other things, such as rural loans, do not involve usurious exploitation. Cooperative enterprises are also being actively promoted. There are a total of sixty-four rural preparatory cooperative societies, providing 30,000 yuan in production funds. The loans released in the first year were fully and voluntarily repaid in the next quarter. The people's credit is also highly admirable.

Regarding education and transportation, I can also briefly describe the general situation. The county has two county-established elementary schools, with 285 students; twelve county-established junior elementary schools, with 367 students; seven district-established elementary schools, with 89 students; five people's schools, with 135 students; seven short-term schools, with 312 students; one private elementary school, with 95 students; twenty-one joint security elementary schools, with 836 students. The number of literate people is 33,390. Regarding transportation, the Yangchong Line and Chongtong Line of the Seven Provinces Highway have already been opened to traffic, and the Chongping Line is still under construction.

The prohibition of opium in Chongyang is a particularly serious issue that must be specially described. Because the people are especially addicted to opium, and the opium is easily transported from Hunan, just taking the corner of the county seat as an example, it is said that there are no fewer than 200 opium dens, large and small. Dasha Ping and Baini Bridge each have more than a dozen. Many young people are also addicted. The county magistrate has strictly prohibited it, sealing up a definite number of opium dens. Currently, there are still 57 dens. In such a small area, there are so many dens, which is shocking. After asking around, no one is willing to say why so many opium dens can be tolerated, or perhaps they have concerns.

Although the people there are mostly lazy and fond of smoking and gambling, their nature is pure and kind, without the tendency to cheat or defraud, which is their virtue. Moreover, they are all unwilling to join the bandits, and they are quite respectful to the county government and the stationed troops. If, after the bandits are suppressed, they diligently cultivate the land, eliminate their addictions, utilize natural products, and improve their manufacturing, the revival of the countryside can be expected. (Sent from Chongyang on the 25th)

Northern Anhui: Promoting Model Irrigation, the Fangqiu Lake Experiment Achieves Success, and the Mingyue Lake Development is Completed

Bengbu Dispatch: Production and construction are the most pressing needs of today, and agricultural experiments are especially imperative. In recent years, the Construction Committee has attached great importance to production enterprises. First, the Model Irrigation General Administration was established in Nanjing to investigate the official wasteland lakes in the country and apply scientific methods to gradually reclaim and plant them, in order to increase production. Wujin and Wujiang in Jiangsu have already achieved considerable success. In northern Anhui, there are many lakes, making it particularly suitable for implementing model irrigation. Since the Fangqiu Lake west of Linhuai was gradually developed by the Fenghuai District Irrigation Experiment Farm two years ago, it has been nearly two years. The lake area is estimated to be over 8,000 mu, and a considerable number of fertile fields have been exposed, which have been gradually cultivated, and production is quite considerable. In order to develop irrigation enterprises, Zhou Chengshu, director of the Linbu Experiment Farm, re-surveyed Mingyue Lake, located about three li southeast of Juli. He immediately started to dig ditches, build embankments, drain water, and install gates for various works. The embankment is about five li long, and there are eight gates. In general, whenever there is a mountain torrent outbreak in the summer and autumn seasons, floods surge south of Fengyang and enter the Huai River from here. The installation of gates can drain the water when opened, so as not to harm agricultural affairs, and it can also store water when closed, so as to irrigate the fields. The above-mentioned construction projects cost more than 10,000 yuan. Now all the works have been completed, and it is planned to carry out experimental reclamation and planting this year. Once it has been successful, it will be invited to be adopted. Reclamation, cultivation, and harvesting will all use new methods, in order to achieve excellent agricultural products, abundant harvests, and increased production benefits. (April 6)

Songjiang: Village Head Arrested for Digging Up Graves

Demolishing tombs and digging up enclosures has been happening from time to time in various districts recently. Previously, Liao Zhaoshun, the town head of Tongbo Town in the first district, submitted a request to prohibit it, and the county government issued a notice to prohibit it. However, recently, villagers Zhong Shiliang and Xu Xingsheng in Xidongjing Township in the second district each had ancestral tombs in Jiangjia Bang in the township. The other day, Zhong Shiliang's nephew, Changsheng, caught sight of someone digging at the tomb and returned to inform his uncle. He immediately reported to the fifth branch station for investigation. It turned out that the village head of the fifth bao in the township, Xu Shiying, had hired Jiangbei people to dig up the tomb. Xu, along with the workers Xie Lijin, Xu Yousan, and others, were brought to the Public Security Bureau for preliminary interrogation. According to Village Head Xu's confession, he hired workers to dig up the tomb because he knew that the tomb was ownerless and planned to use the bricks and stones to repair bridges and roads. However, Zhong and others stated that it was indeed an ancestral tomb and that they had grain documents to prove it. Director He transferred the case to the local court for trial because it was related to the judiciary.

Inspection of the Water and Land Police Team Gathered in Songjiang

The spring inspection of the water and land public security police team of the nine counties under the jurisdiction of Songjiang District has been scheduled to be held on the 11th. The provincial order entrusted the inspection to the administrative inspector, Commissioner Wang Gong. In addition, police inspectors Yang Yuanpei, Shao Qinghuai, Wu Jiqing, and Lin were dispatched to Songjiang to assist in the inspection. The police from various counties and the inspected teams belonging to the first district of the Provincial Waterborne Public Security Team have arrived in Songjiang on the 8th and are stationed in Chaoguosi Temple and the Prison Temple. It is also known that during the inspection, the county magistrates from various counties will come to Songjiang to attend the county magistrate meeting convened by the commissioner's office.

Suzhou: Special Commissioner Sun is Accused Again

Sun Danzhen, the special commissioner of the Wu County Party Affairs, was previously accused by more than 100 party members, including Chen Weizhi, of neglecting his duties. Subsequently, he was accused by more than 40 party members, including Yang Nai, of four counts, including engaging in private interests and corruption. The province is still under investigation. Yesterday (the 8th), Yang Nai and others again presented a report to the Jiangsu Provincial Party Headquarters, stating that Yu Jiuru and others, the executive directors of the Fishermen's Association, had been sentenced to three months in prison by the local court. Sun Danzhen, in order to make up for his own mistakes, published a notice in the newspaper to return the money defrauded from the fishermen in order to shirk his responsibility, which further proves Sun Danzhen's perversion of the law and pursuit of private interests. Moreover, recently he suddenly went to the province or elsewhere, and has no time to take care of his work, which is indeed a neglect of duty. Therefore, they submitted further evidence and requested that he be punished quickly to uphold justice and maintain party discipline.

General Cleanliness Inspection Held in the Urban Area

The third team of the New Life Movement Inspection Group came to Suzhou to inspect the New Life Movement. In recent days, they have been stepping up their work, going to various places in the city and countryside to conduct detailed inspections. According to Captain Wu, they are not satisfied. Yesterday (the 8th) morning, a general cleanliness inspection of the urban area was held, divided into six groups. Each group consisted of one inspector, one military police officer, and one police officer, who set off separately at 8:00 am for inspection and finished at 11:00 am. Starting at 4:00 pm, a call was made for labor service from government officials to clean up the garbage in the streets and alleys of the urban area. The Public Security Bureau has ordered its subordinates since the 8th to notify residents to pay attention to cleanliness in order to emphasize hygiene.

Wuxi: Labor Service Corps Established

The County Construction Bureau established the Wuxi County Construction Bureau New Life Labor Service Corps in accordance with Articles 3 and 4 of the Jiangsu Province General Rules for the Organization of Various Labor Service Corps. All staff members are members of the corps, implementing military, production, and artistic plans. Zhang Lin, director of the bureau, serves as the corps commander, and Huang Dechun serves as the deputy corps commander. It is divided into two teams, each team divided into two groups. The first team leader is Zhu Yingxian, the first group leader is Wang Youcai, the second group leader is Fan Yunpeng, the second team leader is Xu Chuzhen, the first group leader is Qin Xiangtao, and the second group leader is Zhang Mingou. Corps members must perform labor service for one hour every day. The first team is responsible for being punctual, sports, promoting cooperation, utilizing waste materials, promoting the use of domestic goods, helping the elderly, weak, disabled, and injured, holding up the fallen, and saving the hungry, etc. The second team is responsible for opening canals, building dams, planting forests, protecting forests, promoting air defense, promoting science, work-study programs, and social hygiene, etc.

Director Yu Inspects the Police Team

Yu Jingtang, director of the Civil Affairs Department of Jiangsu Province, came to Wuxi at 8:30 pm the night before to inspect the water and land police affairs of Wuxi, Wu County, Changshu, Wujin, Jiangyin, Wujiang, Taicang, and Kunshan, the eight counties in the second district. The inspection was originally scheduled for 8:00 am on the 8th. However, because the weather was unfavorable that morning, with overcast skies and rain, it was decided to postpone it to 1:00 pm at the playground of the Provincial Teachers College in Sheqiao Tou. At around 9:00 am, Director Yu, accompanied by police inspectors Lin Ba, Yang Yuanpei, Wu Jiqing, Shao Qinghuai, and Section Chief Zou Chenhou, technician Zhang Jingshi of the Education Department, and others, inspected various institutions and organizations and expressed satisfaction. At around 1:30 pm, a total of 1,125 people, including the inspected police teams and officials from various counties, gathered at the playground of the Provincial Teachers College. It was then that a strong wind was blowing, followed by heavy rain. The officers stood on both sides of the rostrum, waiting quietly for the lecture. At that time, the wind and rain became even more violent, causing the inspected police officers' clothes to be completely wet, but their spirits were very full, without any fear or shrinking. Then, Director Yu of the Civil Affairs Department and Commissioner Zang gave speeches, with many words of warning and encouragement. After the speeches, it was already 2:00 pm, and they were ordered to return to their original counties to serve. Mr. Yu returned to the province in the evening.

Changshu: Three Female Workers Die in Boat Capsizing

The female worker boat of the Hongqiao Xieji Cloth Factory outside the East Gate suddenly capsized during a thunderstorm yesterday, and all 16 people on the boat fell into the water. As a result, three people died, one of whom was a new bride, which was extremely tragic. It has been verified that the Xieji Cloth Factory was opened by Xu Yongchang. The factory recruits young female workers and has a ferry boat to pick up and drop off female workers in the morning and evening. On the evening of the 7th, 16 female workers were returning home in the same boat. It happened to be a thunderstorm, and the female workers, mostly around 20 years old, were competing for umbrellas to shelter from the rain in the boat. At that time, the tide was surging and rapid, causing the boat to sway and become unstable, and it capsized. All the people fell into the water. After the factory learned the news, they ordered workers to find and retrieve them. As a result, 13 people were rescued, most of whom were barely breathing. There were still three people who had died, and their names are still under investigation. The factory owner has reported to the public security sub-bureau of the township. The next morning (the 8th), he personally came to the city and went to the county to verify.

Yangzhou: Girl Burned to Death in Fire in Shaobo

The home of Hu Daizi, who opened a lantern shop in Zhongda Street, Shaobo Town, Jiangdu, suddenly caught fire at about 8:00 pm the other day. For a time, the whole town was in an uproar, and the fire was bright. Fortunately, the firefighters were able to put out the fire after their effective efforts. It is estimated that two tiled houses were burned down, and a six-year-old girl was burned to death. The fire also affected the Peisheng Hospital next door, burning down a gatehouse. The neighbors were all frightened. It is said that the cause of the fire was due to the old woman's carelessness in cooking dinner, leaving fire in the firewood.

Jiaxing: The Entire County Divided into Districts to Guide Sericulture

Xu Zhaokun, director of the Jiaxing Sericulture General Guidance Institute, and Zheng Genquan, deputy director, said that as Qingming has passed, the villages are preparing to raise silkworms. They have now hired more than 50 instructors and distributed them to the guidance institutes in the villages to work. The entire county has been divided into three rounds of guidance areas. The first area has 10 guidance branches, and the director himself concurrently serves as the instructor. The second area has seven guidance branches, and the instructor is Bangyun. The third area has five guidance offices, and the instructor is Lu Xinxiong. The directors of the guidance branches have also been appointed separately.

Sudden Weather Change, Hail Falls

From noon on the 6th, the weather was abnormally hot and humid. On the morning of the 7th, although there was a thunderstorm, it was still more humid than on the 6th. The summer heat table even reached above 80 degrees. At 4:15 pm, dark clouds covered the sky, and thunder rumbled. Suddenly, hail fell, as large as broad beans, making a banging sound. It stopped after more than ten minutes. Then there was heavy rain, but the humidity was still not reduced. The crops in the countryside, such as beans, wheat, and rapeseed, were damaged a lot.

New Director of the Western Zhejiang Liquor Tax Bureau

Jiang Lutang has been selected by the provincial bureau to serve as the director of the Western Zhejiang Liquor Tax Bureau. After being appointed, Jiang arrived in Jiaxing the day before yesterday to take over the bureau. More than half of the internal staff have been replaced.

Xiaoshan: A Large Number of Hungry People Beg for Food in the Villages

On the afternoon of the 6th, a large number of refugees from Hunan arrived in Dangshan Bay, on the border of Shao and Xiao. Zhu Wengui, the representative of the hungry people, asked the village office to provide food. Because the village office had no funds, it collected more than 400 silver dollars and five dou of white rice from nearby households and distributed them to the refugees, who supported the old and carried the young and went to Yifeng. On the afternoon of the 6th, more than 500 refugees also arrived in Houdu. Fortunately, local gentry raised six silver dollars and five dou of rice, ordering them to go to Anchang.

Local News

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Follows the Reporting Regulations and Will Begin a General Report on Opium Smokers Within the Week; All Opium Paste Shops in the City Will Reissue New Licenses; The Special Commissioner for Opium Prohibition and Reporting, Ma Liang, Will Come to Shanghai

The regulations for reporting opium smokers, formulated by the Opium Prohibition Supervision Department of the Military Affairs Committee, have been sent to the provinces and cities, ordering the competent authorities to implement them. The Municipal Public Security Bureau has now followed these regulations to prepare for the general report on opium smokers. The licenses for opium paste shops in Shanghai for the 24th year of the Republic [1935] have expired, and new licenses will be reissued this month. The number of shops will be reduced during the reissuance. The Special Commissioner for Opium Smoker Reporting of the Military Affairs Committee will come to Shanghai to serve. The "Dagonbao" reporter investigated and reported the details as follows:

Starting the Opium Smoker Reporting Work

The Opium Prohibition Supervision Department of the Military Affairs Committee, in order to eliminate opium smokers within a limited time, drafted the regulations for reporting opium smokers and sent them to the provincial and municipal governments, ordering the competent authorities to comply with and implement them. The Municipal Public Security Bureau has now received the order from the municipal government, and the Fourth Section (Opium Prohibition Section) will, within this week, carry out the reporting procedures according to the items listed in the regulations, preparing to implement a general report on opium smokers throughout the city.

Shanghai Opium Paste Shops Reissue New Licenses

According to a message from the Shanghai Office of the Opium Prohibition Supervision Office of the Military Affairs Committee, there are a total of 12 opium paste shops, 54 Class A opium paste stores, 25 Class B stores, and 1 Class C store in the city. The business licenses for the 24th year of the Republic [1935] have expired and are scheduled to be reissued this month for the 25th year of the Republic [1936] to the municipal government. During the reissuance period, the municipal government will strictly reduce the number of opium paste shops based on the number of registered opium smokers and the amount of opium registered by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. It is also heard that several opium paste shops will be ordered to be closed during the reissuance due to violations of regulations.

Reporting Commissioner Will Come to Shanghai in the Coming Days

The Opium Prohibition Supervision Department has appointed special commissioners for opium administration reporting in six provinces and cities, including Jiangsu, Shanghai, Shandong, Qinghai, Yunnan, and Zhejiang. Ma Liang, the special commissioner for opium administration reporting in Jiangsu Province and Shanghai City, has been dispatched after being appointed. He has already departed to Zhenjiang, Wuxi, and other places to inspect the opium prohibition situation in each county and is scheduled to come to Shanghai in the coming days for inspection. If the competent authorities in charge of opium prohibition in this city fail to perform their duties effectively, they will be reported. If the situation is serious, or if there are acts of favoritism, the local officials in charge of opium administration will be severely punished by the Opium Prohibition Supervision Department.

Tang Haian and Others Saw Him Off

Opening of Ballot Boxes This Afternoon
