Increase in Shanghai Goods Exported to the United States

Slight Decrease in Tea and Sesame

According to statistics released by the U.S. Consulate General, Shanghai's exports to the United States in the first three months of this year totaled US$6,687,273, an increase of US$1,150,000 compared to US$5,521,554 in the same period in 1935. Exports to the Philippines also increased from US$254,953 last year to US$333,489, and exports to Hawaii increased from US$10,752 last year to US$11,112. The largest increase in Shanghai's exports to the United States was in goatskin and lambskin, which increased from US$469,914 in the first three months of last year to US$1,034,458 in the same period this year. However, tea decreased from US$152,948 to US$31,509, and sesame also decreased from US$1,419,805 to US$1,054,712. The increase in exports to the Philippines was mainly in cotton goods.

American Plans to Extend Loans to China

Recommendations from Ferrand and Fox

The Continental News reported that Mr. Ferrand, former president of the American Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai and vice president of the Sin-American Company, recently returned to the United States and had detailed discussions with various economic experts. According to the Chamber's monthly publication, Mr. Ferrand stated that the United States has a plan to immediately subsidize American trade with China. American manufacturers are currently planning to form a consortium with a debt of US$150 million to provide long-term loans for various practical industrial projects in China on a revolving basis, guaranteed by foreign-style banking organizations. In addition, Mr. Fox, the director of the recent American Economic Survey Mission to China, is currently planning to organize a company to take over the various debts owed by the Chinese government to Americans. It is heard that Mr. Fox has obtained a tentative promise that if he can organize a company to settle these debts, the Chinese government will be able to repay US$6 million annually, but the payments must be used to purchase American goods. Mr. Ferrand also stated that American exports to various countries have decreased from $5 billion to $1.6 billion annually, so manufacturers are eager to find ways to remedy this, and the U.S. government has also extended loans to the Export-Import Bank, believing that this will enable American exporters to compete with foreign countries in export trade.

Tricolor Wheel Fire Extinguished: Ship Intact, Cargo in Five Holds Destroyed

Reuters, San Francisco, 8th: According to a recent telegram, the fire on the Norwegian motor vessel Tricolor has been extinguished, so the lives of the crew should be safe. The ship encountered an accident on its way from Manila to California. Last night's telegrams stated that the fifth hold was still burning and requested assistance from nearby ships. Today's telegram states that although the fire has been extinguished, it does not mention whether assistance is still needed.

Tianjin Goods Completely Destroyed

The reporter of this newspaper continued to report the following based on the investigation yesterday: The goods loaded on the Tricolor from the ports of Tianjin and Shanghai were all in the fifth hold. Tianjin goods were in the lower hold, and Shanghai goods were in the upper hold. The fire broke out in the fifth hold. Fortunately, the 700 tons of tung oil from Shanghai were not loaded, otherwise the entire ship would have been unimaginable. It is now known that after two days and nights of burning, all the goods shipped to the United States from Shanghai and Tianjin have been completely destroyed.

Ship Preserved

Shanghai Tianxiang Foreign Firm sent many telegrams to inquire about the whereabouts of the ship, but never received a direct reply from the ship. Later, they telegraphed the Hong Kong firm to inquire nearby. Finally, they received confirmation that the remaining fire in the fifth hold had gradually been extinguished by the efforts of the entire crew. Although the fourth and sixth holds were not affected by the fire, the goods may have suffered water damage. Fortunately, the hull of the ship has been preserved. It is planned to instruct the shipowner to try to sail to Yokohama for major repairs in the dock. If it is not possible to go to Japan, then change to Honolulu. Telegrams have been sent to notify.

Ship's History

The original Tricolor was pledged by the British government last year. Later, due to an accident en route, the entire ship was destroyed. The British government and the insurance company paid out compensation, and the William Babur Shipping Company used this compensation to build a new ship, which was still named Tricolor, but the carrying capacity had been expanded to 11,000 tons, and the steel plate hull was very good. It had only been in operation for five months when it caught fire. This ship was originally managed by Shunheng Foreign Firm in this port, but it was temporarily replaced by Tianxiang due to the decision to take over the Taiyin route.

Foreign Directors Election of the Public Concession: Thorough Investigation of Vote Counting Errors Shows the Cause Was a Simple Oversight; Relevant Personnel Were Not Intentionally Negligent

Regarding the vote counting error that occurred during the recent election of foreign directors of the Public Concession Municipal Council, the Council appointed the current directors of the Council, Caneke Kelleri and Yamamoto Takeo, etc. as a three-person investigative committee to thoroughly investigate the incident of the error occurring. Since the committee started its investigation on the 30th of last month, it has now reported the incident. Here is a summary of its report to the Board of Directors:

The original text is very long, totaling fourteen pages. The following is a summary of its conclusions: "Based on the findings of this committee's investigation, the responsibility for the omission of the failure to fully count the votes should be shared by the two vote counters, the Director-General of the Municipal Council, and the Deputy Director of the Finance Department (Head of the Revenue Department)." In order to prevent similar incidents from occurring in the future, the committee also proposed that the new Board of Directors this year should instruct the personnel of the Municipal Council to formulate new regulations within the scope of the Land Regulations, stipulating the procedures for elections and vote counting, and the responsibilities and tasks of each office worker. In addition, the committee also proposed that the term "Election Reporter" for the Director-General of the Municipal Council, as stated in the current "Service Regulations" of the Municipal Council, is only mentioned in the resolution of the 1925 Taxpayer Annual Meeting, and is not stipulated by the Land Regulations, and is very different from the duties and status of the so-called "Election Reporter" in the United Kingdom, so it is proposed to delete the term. Furthermore, there are many unclear boundaries between the duties and responsibilities of senior officials of the Municipal Council inquired during the investigation. Although this section is not within the scope of the investigation of this election matter, it is essential. Therefore, it is also proposed to ask the new Board of Directors to form another committee to investigate and define the responsibilities and tasks of senior officials of the Municipal Council.

Scope of Investigation: The scope of the task of this investigation committee can be roughly divided into the following three items: Investigate the cause of the omission in vote counting in this election of foreign directors; Ascertain the responsibilities of the relevant personnel; and Propose how to improve the election mechanism in the future. Based on the above scope, the committee began its investigation work. The personnel consulted included the two vote counters, Wilson and Borson; the personnel of the Municipal Council included Director-General Zhong Si, Deputy Director of the Finance Department (Head of the Revenue Department) Born, Accountant of the Finance Department Mitton, Senior Assistant Kao Maolan, Japanese Assistant Chief Ishuku Hidenen, Assistant of the Director-General's Office Pissley, and Assistant of the Finance Department Klein. The above persons were all present during the vote counting, and Zhong Si was present at the beginning of the vote counting, at the end of the vote counting, and at intervals in between.

Cause of Error: According to the report of the Investigation Committee, "After hearing all the testimonies, the committee firmly believes that the error in the count of this vote was entirely due to negligence. All the evidence obtained does not raise the slightest suspicion of misconduct on the part of each relevant person. However, since the error has occurred, the lack of command in the deliberation hall, the place where the votes are counted, is indeed undeniable." The report further stated, "This lack of command is due to the fact that the responsibilities and tasks of each person present were not clearly defined."

Analysis of Responsibilities: According to the provisions of the Land Regulations, the responsibility for handling the election should be borne by the two vote counters. However, according to the committee's investigation, the vote counters did not understand their responsibilities and tasks beforehand. They claimed that they did not check whether the two ballot boxes were completely empty when counting the votes. They dare not escape their responsibility for this. However, there were so many senior officials of the Municipal Council present at the same time, so they all thought that others must have paid attention to this matter. According to many years of established practice, the vote counters' assumption seems to be reasonable. But on the other hand, since the vote counters have received the responsibility, how can they never study the tasks stipulated by the Land Regulations? Therefore, the investigation committee deeply felt that "these two vote counters, technically speaking, should bear the responsibility for the error. However, under the circumstances at the time, the Director-General of the Municipal Council and the Head of the Revenue Department cannot shirk their responsibilities." As for the responsibility of the Head of the Revenue Department, according to his own understanding, it originally ended at 3:00 PM on the second afternoon of the election, when the ballot boxes were handed over to the vote counters. However, according to many years of established practice, the officer always stayed in the vote counting hall afterwards to assist the work of the vote counters. This kind of assistance was indeed regarded as indispensable for the sake of quick handling, and because of his assistance, the scope of the vote counters' responsibilities was covered up a lot. Therefore, in fact, the officer has assumed part of the responsibility of commanding the vote counting. Therefore, the committee deeply felt that "although this work of the Head of the Revenue Department came from habit, he should also share the responsibility for the occurrence of this error." As for the duties of the Director-General, if we look at the provisions of the Land Regulations, they are limited to representing the Municipal Council to notify the election of two officials and the vote counting of two vote counters. However, according to the resolution of the 1925 Taxpayer Annual Meeting, in order to maintain the secrecy of the election voting, the Director-General has the responsibility to burn the ballots afterwards. Other responsibilities actually assumed by the Director-General include the sealing of empty ballot boxes before the election, the subsequent meeting with the vote counters, the delivery of the keys to the ballot boxes, and the publication of the election results. However, according to the records, the responsibilities of the Director-General to the vote counters, as stipulated by the Land Regulations, have never been explained at the time of appointment. Therefore, to remedy this, the clauses of the Land Regulations regarding this matter should be attached when appointing vote counters in the future. Furthermore, the Director-General does not need to be present at the vote counting. What he should do is only to meet the vote counters before the vote counting starts, hand over the keys, and accept their report after the vote counting ends. However, also due to many years of practice, the Director-General always goes to the scene for a short time to inspect during the vote counting, and since 1933, the time of the Director-General's inspection has also increased, and this year is particularly so. According to the Director-General's statement, the purpose of this is only for assistance, but the committee deeply feels that "his stay in the vote counting hall, due to the lack of definition of his position, and the simultaneous presence of another senior official of the Municipal Council, with several assistants each, is the cause of the lack of command. Therefore, the officer has to share the responsibility for the occurrence of the error." All other personnel were subordinates of the Director-General and the Head of the Revenue Department and were ordered to come. Since there were no defined tasks, they were only assisting at any time.

Other Parts: The important parts of the investigation report also include the detailed methods for improving the election and vote counting procedures, the detailed rules for the responsibilities and tasks of the election personnel, and the clauses of the Land Regulations regarding elections, the resolution of the 1925 Taxpayer Annual Meeting regarding the secrecy of elections, and the procedures handled over the years. Due to the limited space, it is not possible to record them all.

Ministry of Industry's Fishing Market: Inaugural Meeting Tomorrow

The Ice and Fresh Fish Industry's Decision to Participate is No Longer a Problem

The New News Agency reported that the Ministry of Industry, in order to control the fishing industry and relieve fishermen, has built a large fish market in Zhoujiazuidao, Yangshupu, Shanghai. The entire project was completed in November last year, but it has not yet opened due to unresolved organizational issues. After several consultations between Wu Dingchang, Minister of Industry, and Shanghai gentry and businessmen Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Shenzhi, and Lin Kanghou, it was decided to jointly operate the market by officials and businessmen, with a capital of 1.2 million national currency, divided into 12,000 shares, each share being 100 yuan. Officials and businessmen each account for half. Currently, the official shares of 600,000 have been fully paid by the Ministry of Industry. As for the business shares, except for the 150,000 yuan from the ice and fresh fish industry, which is to be decided today, the river fresh fish industry has already subscribed for 50,000 yuan. Another 100,000 yuan has been temporarily borrowed from the Bank of Communications, and the remaining 300,000 yuan will be fully subscribed by the Shanghai business community.

Ice and Fresh Fish Participate: The Ice and Fresh Fish Industry Association of this city initially strongly supported the principle of the Ministry of Industry's official-business joint venture fish market. However, more than 3,000 employees were deeply afraid that their livelihoods would be panicked after the opening of the fish market, so they put forward six points to request remedies. It is now learned that the association convened an emergency meeting yesterday afternoon. After discussion, it was decided to participate with only some trivial issues. After negotiating and deciding today, they will subscribe for shares and join. Therefore, the opposition of the ice and fresh fish industry is no longer a problem.

Shareholders' Meeting: The inaugural meeting of the shareholders of the Shanghai Fishing Market Co., Ltd. of the Ministry of Industry will be held at the China & South Sea Bank at 11:00 AM tomorrow (the 10th). The outside rumors that the shareholders' meeting would be held today are not accurate. As for the meeting location and time, it remains to be decided today. At that time, in addition to mutually electing eleven directors and five supervisors, the Ministry of Industry will appoint one person as chairman from the standing directors, and discuss the opening date and all preparatory matters. Official and business shareholders Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Shen Tianxin, etc. are all prepared to attend. The Ministry of Industry has sent the Director of the Fisheries and Animal Husbandry Department to Shanghai to participate.

Preparing for Opening: The fish market is scheduled to officially open for business on the 19th of this month, but it must be approved by the shareholders' inaugural meeting on the 10th. As for the various projects of the market's buildings, such as cold storage, market, and floating dock, etc., they have been completed. The office and business places have also been arranged. The market's business methods will adopt a public auction system so that prices are uniform, eliminate manipulation and suppression, and gradually reduce the burden on depressed merchants and fishermen, and implement the rescue of China's endangered fishing industry.

Cotton Industry Control Committee: Relieving Cotton Areas Nationwide

Distributing 2,100 Tons of High-Quality Cotton Seeds; Improving Ginning and Adopting Saw-Tooth Gins

According to Shen Shi News Agency, Shandong, Henan, Hebei, Shaanxi and other places in China are cotton-producing areas, with an annual output of about 110,000 dan. However, last year, Shandong, Henan, and Hubei provinces suffered from both drought and floods, and many cotton seeds were not sown. The output of various provinces across the country also decreased. Therefore, improving cotton production and revitalizing rural areas are urgent priorities. Mr. Ma Guangwen, a cotton expert from the Commodity Inspection Bureau, told a reporter from Shen Shi News Agency about the Cotton Industry Control Committee's methods for relieving cotton farmers this year, which are recorded below:

Improving Cotton Seeds

In view of the fact that cotton seeds in various parts of China have gradually decreased each year due to poor storage by cotton farmers in the past, or mixed with inferior seeds, if high-quality seeds are not replaced in time, the cotton harvest in our country may be affected. This spring, the association specifically purchased 2,100 tons of S-type No. 4 cotton seeds from the United States, which arrived in Shanghai in March. In order to prevent the American cotton boll weevil from harming cotton, in order to prevent diseases and pests from American cotton, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau was ordered to fumigate and disinfect, and the cotton control association transported them to various provinces for distribution.

Relieving Cotton Farmers

The focus of relieving cotton-producing areas is mostly on the provinces in North China, because there is less rainfall in North China, and the weather and geography are suitable for planting cotton, which is better than provinces such as Jiangsu, Anhui, and Zhejiang. Therefore, this association will use most of the 2,100 tons of cotton seeds to relieve cotton-producing areas in Shaanxi, Henan, Hubei, and Shandong. The cotton seeds were fully distributed to various provinces last month.

Improving Ginning

China's industry is backward, and most machines are used in the old style. For example, the cotton gins used in various places, except for the roller gins used in Shanghai, Hankou and other places, are mostly foot-operated iron machines. It is difficult to select high-quality seeds after ginning with this kind of bad machine, and the cotton fiber is broken by the gin. In order to maintain the high-quality cotton seeds in various cotton-producing areas and improve the quality, the Cotton Industry Control Association plans to imitate the Egyptian cotton ginning method and purchase the latest steam flow saw-tooth cotton gins. It is heard that ginning with this machine can keep the cotton fiber in its original state, and the cotton seeds are not damaged.

Instructions from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce: Questions Regarding Affixing Stamps to Packing Lists, etc.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, in a letter yesterday to the Gongji Glass Factory, responded to questions regarding affixing stamps to packing lists, etc., stating:

In response to your letter of the 7th of this month inquiring about stamp tax matters, we hereby provide the following itemized answers:

Both packing lists and loading slips are used to notify customers to inspect and receive goods when they are sent out. Therefore, based on their nature, they are considered invoices and should be stamped accordingly.

Article 17 of the Stamp Tax Law states that if the amount is not specified, the highest tax rate for the type of item listed should be applied. Therefore, if the invoice does not specify the price of the goods, it should be stamped at the highest rate of two cents. It is still advisable to list the price after the invoice is issued. If the price is not listed and a flat two-cent stamp is affixed, inspectors will still consider the stamp insufficient and impose a fine.

Shipping and allocation documents used internally between the factory and the warehouse are considered internal documents as defined in Article 3, Section 8 of the Stamp Tax Law. These documents do not create external rights or obligations and are different in nature from invoices and receipts used externally to obtain goods. Therefore, according to the law, they do not need to be stamped. Furthermore, according to the Ministry of Finance's decree No. 7213 dated September 21 of last year, it is also stated that for warehouses, factories, issuing offices, or branches of various businesses, although there may be a distinction between headquarters and branches, if their capital and operations are not independent but are in fact part of the same organization, then documents used for internal notification do not create external rights or obligations and do not need to be stamped. The regulations are clear and can be followed accordingly.

Frequent Spring Rains: Stagnant Sales of Various Rice and Grains

Rice Prices Fall by More Than 20 Cents

The Dagong Agency reports: Sales of rice and grain are usually sluggish around the Qingming Festival, commonly known as the "Spring Plague Festival." Due to frequent spring rains after the festival, the number of rice boats arriving in Shanghai from Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, Kunshan, Qingpu, Zhangjiagang, and other inland areas has decreased. There are only 30 to 40 boats at the wharves in the north and south of the city.

The total cargo is 60 dan, and the number of orders from merchants in Qingdao, Tianjin, Weihaiwei, and other areas is also not high. Therefore, rice prices in Shanghai have been slightly affected and have fallen by more than 20 cents in recent days. Yesterday, the opening prices on the morning and afternoon markets were $10.78 for Changbang Grade 1 rice and $8.50 to $9.30 for Grade 2 rice. The market price for Hunan indica rice remained stable with no increase or decrease. However, the sales volume of Bo rice is showing the most improvement.

Report on the Disaster in Chuxian, Anhui

The China Jisen Association has received a report from various legal entities in Chuxian County, Anhui Province, including the county party department, the disaster relief committee, the chamber of commerce, the farmers' association, and the finance committee, stating that Chuxian is strategically important but has suffered repeated military disasters since the Revolution. It was then ravaged by bandits in the northwest for over a decade, with thousands of villages plundered. This was followed by famine, leaving the rural areas bankrupt. The drought in 1934 and 1935 resulted in a harvest of less than 20%. People are fleeing everywhere, crying with hunger. Fortunately, there was little rain and snow last winter, so people were able to support the elderly and young and seek food in the south of the Yangtze River, barely surviving. Now that mid-spring has passed, farming is in full swing. Tens of thousands of disaster-stricken farmers, sent back from the capital, have no food, no clothing, no oxen, and no seeds. Their homes are empty, and smoke has ceased to rise from their chimneys. If spring farming is not carried out, what can be hoped for from the autumn harvest? In recent days, the number of disaster victims gathering and seeking relief has increased daily. There are indeed more than 60,000 people who will not survive without relief. Yesterday, the Third District Office of the county reported that in Sanxingji in the west of the county, families are starving to death in the streets of Jiuzhou, a sight that makes passersby weep. We beg you to provide the nectar of mercy and provide large-scale relief. The association previously received reports of severe disasters from Hubei, Anhui, Henan, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Sichuan, and other provinces, which were reported in previous issues. Now, we have received a report from Chuxian describing an extremely severe disaster. With the spring famine in full swing, we hope that benevolent people will open their purses to provide relief, saving people from death and restoring them to life. The merit is immeasurable, and the rewards are beyond comprehension.

You gentlemen are all knowledgeable members of society, or leaders in various industries. Chinese Detective Illegally Arrests Person Across Border: French Concession Taxpayers' Association Negotiates

Requests Letter to French Municipal Council Demanding Chen Chengkun Be Transferred to Court

Huang Jiande, a clerk from the Jin Yu Law Firm at No. 68 Ningbo Road in the French Concession and a native of Suzhou, has been working there for two years. Unexpectedly, at 9:30 AM on the 7th (the day before yesterday), Chen Chengkun, a Chinese detective from the Public Concession police, went directly to Jin's law firm to arrest Huang Jiande. Chen claimed that Huang's cousin, Huang Dong, who works at Lao Jie Fu on Nanjing Road, was suspected of stealing forty yuan recently. He was taken to the Lujiawan police station in the French Concession. After the police station brought the defendant Huang Dong for questioning, it was found that Huang Jiande was not involved and was immediately released, which has been reported in various newspapers. It is now learned that Lawyer Jin believes that the detective abused his power to detain Huang and requested the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association yesterday to negotiate with the French Concession authorities based on reason. After receiving the letter, the Taxpayers' Association wrote to the French Municipal Council yesterday, requesting that Chen Chengkun be transferred to the court. The original letter is recorded as follows: "Regarding the letter from Chinese Committee Member Jin Liren stating that at 9:30 this morning, Chen Chengkun, a Chinese detective claiming to be from the British Concession police, suddenly came to our firm and illegally detained our clerk Huang Jiande at the French General Police Station. At the time, we were completely unaware of the reason. After investigation, it was said that his cousin, Huang Lian, was suspected of stealing cloth from the store. As British Concession detective Chen Chengkun did not consult with the French Concession police and did not present an arrest warrant, he illegally crossed the border and arrested a citizen without authorization, which has a significant impact on the public security of the concession residents. In addition to separately submitting requests to the French Consul General and the Director General of the French General Police Station to seriously negotiate with the British Concession police authorities in accordance with the law, and transferring the British Concession detective Chen Chengkun who illegally arrested the citizen and our firm's clerk Huang Jiande to the Second Special District Local Court for fair and lawful handling, we are reporting the situation of the British Concession detective's illegal arrest of the citizen in detail, hoping that your association will investigate and negotiate with the French authorities based on reason to reassure the law-abiding and deter the lawless, etc. In accordance with Article 8 of the Law of the Tutelage Period of the Republic of China, citizens shall not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished without due process of law, and Article 10 of the same law stipulates that citizens' residences shall not be entered, searched, or sealed without due process of law. However, Chen Chengkun, a Chinese detective claiming to be from the British Concession police, dared to enter a citizen's residence and illegally arrest a person without authorization. Our association deeply regrets this. Furthermore, even if Huang Jiande were suspected of theft, he should be summoned for questioning in accordance with the law, and even with a court warrant, the French Concession police should be consulted before making an arrest, which is the legal procedure. However, Chen Chengkun arrested the citizen without authorization and without due process of law. Such disregard for the law must be severely punished to serve as a warning. Fortunately, Chinese Committee Member Jin deeply understands the law, and the clerk Huang Jiande was not wrongly accused. In order to uphold the law, our association requests that your council order the Director General of the General Police Station to transfer Chen Chengkun to the court for investigation and also seriously negotiate with the Public Concession authorities to prevent such incidents from happening again. This is of utmost importance. This is addressed to the French Concession Municipal Council." At the same time, a letter was sent to the Public Concession Taxpayers' Association, which forwarded it to the Public Concession Standing Bureau for negotiation, etc.

Small Trading Activities: Copper Coin Prices Rise

Exchange Rate of One Yuan to 480 Copper Coins

In recent days, due to sporadic small trading activities in the market, coupled with the need for copper coins for buying cotton powder, purchasing silkworm eggs, and sericulture in rural areas, the price of copper coins has gradually increased again. The usual exchange rate is 3,000 copper coins per yuan, while double dimes are exchanged at twelve cents. Many exchange shops offer twelve cents less ten cash. Double dimes are exchanged at 490, and some shops offer 490. Single dimes are exchanged at 480 cash. In bustling areas, the rate is only ten cents and 480 cash, or even only 450 cash. Tobacco shops, in order to make a small profit, are creating various schemes to attract business, leading to many disputes. Also, the copper coin exchange rate opened yesterday in the money market was 302,000 cash, an increase of 4,000 cash compared to two weeks ago.

Woman Crushed in Two by Locomotive

At the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway South Station, a locomotive was released at 9:00 AM yesterday to the Rihui Port Station. Unexpectedly, when the locomotive passed through Dapu Road (i.e., Wai Yangqi) on the track, a woman in her thirties was walking there, crossing the tracks, and was unable to avoid the locomotive, resulting in her being crushed in two. The sight was unbearable, and she died instantly. The driver immediately reported to the stationmaster, who sent police officers to investigate. The Railway Police Department of the South Station is investigating. The deceased was Cao, the wife of Xu Laowu, age thirty-five, residing at Shengji Garden on Zhizaoju Road outside the West Zha Lan. She was walking along the road at 8:30 AM yesterday when she was crushed to death. The police department instructed the local bailiff Gu Xuepu to report to the local court for examination. At 5:00 PM yesterday, the court sent a prosecutor to conduct the examination, which confirmed that she was crushed to death by the train. In addition to filling out the death certificate, her husband, Xu Laowu, received 20 yuan in coffin expenses from the Railway Bureau, and the bailiff prepared the coffin for burial.

Brothers Eat Puffer Fish Together, One Brother in Danger, One Dies

Chen Dalang, age fifty-six, and Chen Sanlang, age fifty-three, natives of Chongming, are siblings who work for a living and are able to make ends meet. Their children and grandchildren are also grown and self-sufficient. Yesterday afternoon, the Chen brothers, in their desire for delicious food, purchased several puffer fish and brought them home. They also bought a bottle of alcohol, cooked the fish, and drank. Unexpectedly, both of them mistakenly ate the fish roe. By midnight, they were critically ill. Fortunately, their family noticed and rushed them to the hospital for treatment. Chen Sanlang died ten minutes after arriving at the hospital due to severe poisoning, while Chen Dalang is also in critical condition.

Robbers Murder Victim in Yangsi Bridge, Pudong

Three Robbers, Each Wielding Iron Bars, Tie Up Everyone's Hands; Old Woman Shouts, is Stabbed in Throat, Suffocates and Dies

—Plunder Lasts for Three Hours—

A robbery occurred in Lujiayan, Yangsi District, Pudong, the night before last, resulting in the victim's death. The details are recorded below. Zhou Jinlan, a local resident of No. 3 Lujiayan, northeast of Yangsi Bridge in Yangsi District, Pudong, works as a cook at Zheng Yixing Niupihao in the South City Dama Tou. His son, Zhou Jinfa, works as a salesman at the Da Zhonghua Shoe Lace Factory in Dama Tou and does not often return to the village. The day before yesterday, Zhou Jinfa took leave to return home for the Qingming Festival to sweep the ancestral tombs. Everyone went to bed at night. Unexpectedly, at around 11:00 PM that night, several robbers came to the Zhou house, broke open the side door, and three robbers entered, each wielding an iron bar. The others stood guard outside. They first broke into Zhou Jinfa's bedroom, tied up Jinfa and his wife with ropes, and silenced them. Then, they broke into the adjacent bedroom of Jinlan's cousin, Zhou Jiyu, followed by the bedroom of Jiyu's son, Zhou Haigen, and tied them up in the same way. Then, they drove Zhou Jinfa and his wife into Zhou Jiyu's room, where one robber guarded them, while two robbers returned to Zhou Jinlan's bedroom. Zhou's wife, Zhou Xi (age fifty-two), woke up in her sleep upon hearing the noise and shouted for help. The two robbers, angered by her shouting, rushed forward and grabbed her throat, tying her arms with grass ropes. As she was old and weak, she was unable to struggle. After a while, she suffocated and died. The robbers then divided up and searched for three hours, carrying away the stolen goods. After the robbers left, those who had been tied up were able to free themselves. Zhou Jinfa went to his mother Zhou Xi's room to check on the situation and found her lying on the bed, already dead. Upon inspecting the surrounding bedrooms, a total of 108 yuan in legal tender, one gold chain, one silver chain, one gold ring, three gold buttons, one silver watch, one flannel shirt, one flannel vest, and one woolen twill trousers were stolen. Zhou Jinfa reported to the Yangsi Bridge Police Station and requested that the robbers be arrested. Officer Xiao Jingfu of the station led police officers to search in all directions, but as the robbers had been gone for a long time, they were nowhere to be found. He then returned to the victim's house to investigate. An iron bar, a blue cloth short shirt, a dark blue hat, two pawn tickets, and two pairs of trousers were found in the room and taken back to the police station. The situation was reported to the Tangqiao Police Station for review. Yesterday morning, the local bailiff Xie Zhaogen of the 10th and 11th districts was instructed to report to the local court prosecutor's office for examination. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Lei Binzhang and Inspector Shen Qixiu were commissioned to cross the river to Pudong for the examination.

Yesterday's Gloomy Weather, Strong Winds and Rain

Sudden Drop in Temperature: River and Sea Vessels Obstructed

Since the thunderstorms the day before yesterday, the city has experienced continuous rain throughout the night. The eaves dripped all night long. Yesterday, the sky began to clear after dawn. Around 8:00 AM, sunlight even broke through. Before long, the sky clouded over again. By noon, dark clouds gathered from all directions, making it as dark as dusk. Lights had to be turned on indoors, and vehicles on the streets drove slowly. It was difficult to see clearly more than a few steps away, as if it were night. At the same time, strong winds roared, and windows rattled. Pedestrians rushed along, holding their heads and hats. Around 1:00 PM, heavy rain began to fall, lasting until 3:00 PM in the afternoon, while the strong winds have not stopped until this morning, and the weather has turned cold.

Winds Block River Ships

The weather was bad in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River yesterday morning. A low-pressure system passed through from 32 degrees north latitude and 119 degrees east longitude, bringing strong winds and heavy rain. By noon, it reached Shanghai and entered the Yangtze River, causing strong winds and heavy rain in Wuhu. The river surface was turbulent with waves, and all ships in Wuhu were obstructed. All loading and unloading operations were suspended. The shipping companies received telegrams, and the situation only subsided slightly in the evening.

Fog Blocks Sea Ships

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haiyuan ship, which departed from Shanghai for Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou on the afternoon of the 7th, encountered extremely strong winds and heavy fog at around 4:00 AM yesterday in the sea area near Tanting Island. The ship's navigation was very dangerous. It anchored and stopped sailing. After the wind subsided slightly, it resumed its journey. However, when it approached the sea area near Steep Island, the weather became even worse. Fearing danger, the Haiyuan ship anchored to avoid the wind and fog and telegraphed Shanghai for information. Various sea ships arriving in Shanghai from South China and those exporting from Shanghai were also obstructed by the fog along the way.

Shengjing Ship's Russian Policeman Kicking a Laborer to Death: Trial Concludes

Sentence to be Pronounced on the 14th

Kexin (transliteration), a Russian policeman escorting cargo on the Taikoo Company's Shengjing ship, kicked a laborer named Afu to death while trying to expel him. Tang Rushou, a prosecutor from the local court, examined the body and confirmed that Afu died from his injuries. Kexin was arrested and interrogated, and a public prosecution was filed against him for causing death by injury under Article 277, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. At 3:00 PM yesterday, Judge Wu Deyi presided over the third trial in the Criminal Court. The defendant hired lawyer Wu Kaisheng to appear in court on his behalf. First, the testimony of Cheng Yongnian, an investigator from the water police, was presented, followed by the testimony of Zhang Maosheng, age forty, a native of Ningbo and a dock worker. He testified that around 7:00 PM on March 22nd, he was expelled by the defendant on the Shengjing ship and kicked violently five times. The deceased, Afu, was our companion and was also kicked violently four times by the defendant. He fell from the ladder and died within half an hour. Judge Wu ordered the detained Kexin to be brought to the case for questioning. Kexin, age thirty-five, a Russian national working as a security guard on the Shengjing ship, stated that on the evening in question, while he was on duty, he saw six or seven dock workers sleeping on the deck. He expelled them, only using his feet to push them away and chase them away, and did not kick them violently. He asked for clarification. At this point, Prosecutor Tang entered the court and presented his prosecution. The debate then began and was considered concluded. The sentence was scheduled to be pronounced at 10:00 AM on the 14th of this month, and the defendant was remanded in custody.

Lawyer He Ji Detained in Connection with Fraud and Defamation Case

Someone Sues in Wuxian Local Court; Result: Surrendered Himself with Two Shop Guarantees

Lawyer He Ji, styled Zhuowei, is fifty-seven years old this year, a native of Yiwu, Zhejiang. In May of the 21st year of the Republic (1932), he became a member of the Shanghai Lawyers' Association and established his office on the fifth floor of the Dalu Department Store on Nanjing Road. He lives at No. 98 Huayuanfang, Rue du Père Robert in the French Concession. Recently, Zhu Xiongwu and others filed a lawsuit in the Wuxian Local Court, accusing He Ji of fraud and defamation. He Ji is suspected of being involved in the case, so the Wuxian Local Court secretly telegraphed the Shanghai Second Special Court to assist in summoning him the day before yesterday. After receiving the telegram, the court notified the judicial advisory office yesterday to dispatch Jingmu Mai Wenjin to arrest He at his address. He was arrested and sent to the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court at 4:00 PM in the afternoon. First, the Jingmu stated that when he was ordered to make the arrest, the defendant He Ji claimed that his name was Wu Jinsheng, not He Ji, and that He Ji had already left and was not in Shanghai. Fortunately, someone pointed out that he was He Ji before he was arrested. When questioned, He Ji said, "I have already sent a letter to the Wuxian Local Court stating that I would surrender myself immediately." The official asked why he denied being He Ji when the Jingmu came to arrest him. He replied that it was a temporary mistake. Chen, a lawyer acting on his behalf, stated that he was allowed to be released on bail to surrender himself. Judge Li Changnian ordered He Ji to provide two guarantees from chain shops to appear in court and ordered him to surrender himself to the Wuxian Local Court for questioning.

Impersonating a Prostitute as a Daughter to Extort Money from a Brothel

Zhou Hongbao is Confirmed to Have Committed Fraud; Father and Son Qu Shuangxi Seemingly Deceived

Wang Zhangshi, a 42-year-old brothel owner from Suzhou, operates a brothel at No. 17 Bing'an Lane, Avenue Edward VII, in the French Concession. She employs over a dozen prostitutes who, as soon as the lanterns light up, go to entertainment venues to solicit customers. On the 6th, a man from Jiangbei named Zhou Hongbao, 41 years old, residing at No. 17 Tongyu Lane, Luban Road, Nanshi, accompanied by his fellow townsman Qu Shuangxi, 51 years old, and Qu Mujin, 24 years old, a father and son, went to the brothel. They claimed that the prostitute Jin Di, 18 years old, was Qu Shuangxi's biological daughter who had been abducted and sold into prostitution two years ago. They demanded a ransom of 300 yuan for her release, threatening drastic measures otherwise. They negotiated at Room 30, Chunjiang Hotel, Xinxinqiao Street. Brothel owner Wang Zhangshi outwardly agreed but secretly reported to the police. Detective Zhou Bingcheng and Bao Tan Xu Jinlong were dispatched to Chunjiang Hotel, where they arrested Zhou and the two Qu's. Yesterday, they were brought before the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. First, police lawyer Yuan Jiahong presented the case, followed by brothel owner Wang Zhangshi recounting the events. When questioned, Zhou Hongbao claimed that a relative, Qu Shuangxi, had a daughter abducted a few years ago and asked him to help find her. Coincidentally, the person saw the plaintiff's slave girl Jin Di at the Great World entertainment center, resembling Qu Shuangxi's lost daughter. Therefore, the person reported to the Qu father and son, who came to Shanghai to identify her, but the identification was negative, and the matter was dropped. Suddenly, an unknown Ying A'er came forward and told the person that brothel owner Zhangshi was willing to pay to settle the matter. Therefore, the person accompanied the Qu father and son to Room 30, Chunjiang Hotel, to negotiate. He provided evasive answers. Qu Shuangxi and Qu Mujin, father and son, both stated that Zhou Hongbao had indeed asked them to come to Shanghai to identify the prostitute. However, they had never identified Jin Di as the lost daughter and had not threatened or extorted the plaintiff. They were simply deceived by Zhou. The police lawyer stated that the first defendant had been proven to have committed extortion, but the criminal suspicion of the second and third defendants could not be proven, requesting a lawful investigation. Judge Li Changnian ruled to detain Zhou Hongbao, while Qu Shuangxi and Qu Mujin, father and son, were released on bail, with temporary detention for those unable to provide bail. The verdict is scheduled for the 11th.

Qingpu Tax Collector Lin Hongru Arrested

Accused of Embezzling Three Thousand Yuan in Taxes; to be Escorted to Qingpu for Interrogation

Lin Hongru, a 38-year-old native of Qingpu, served as a tax collector for the Qingpu County Government. In August of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), the Qingpu County Government Tax Collection Office was ordered to be abolished, and Lin was dismissed. He resided at No. 51 Hongrui Lane, Changsha Road, in the Shanghai Public Concession. Recently, the Qingpu County Government discovered that Lin Hongru had embezzled three thousand yuan in taxes during his tenure and issued a warrant to the Shanghai First Special District Court, which was handed over to the Xinzha Police Station. Yesterday morning at 10:30, Huatan Ruan Yao was specially dispatched to No. 51 Hongrui Lane, Changsha Road, to arrest Lin and detain him at the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin presented the above information. When questioned, Lin Hongru stated that he had served as a tax collector for the county government since April of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), with a monthly salary of only sixteen yuan. In August of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), the agency was ordered to be abolished, and he was dismissed. All the agency's account books were not handed over to the director. The current director, Wu, was reportedly also detained. The missing three thousand yuan was not embezzled but was a shortfall in payment. He is currently suffering from severe tuberculosis and requested temporary admission to a hospital. Judge Wu Zehan reviewed the confession and ruled that Lin Hongru should be transferred for further investigation, with notification to the Qingpu County Government to send police to escort him. Before the transfer, he was temporarily detained at the police station's patrol hospital pending pickup.

Jointly Issued Round-Trip Tickets for Sightseeing and Transportation

Effective May 1st

To facilitate passengers and increase business, the Railway Bureau plans to issue round-trip tickets for sightseeing and transportation between passenger transportation stations, effective May 1st of this year. It also plans to jointly issue third-class, one-way, special-price ordinary passenger tickets between the North and South Shanghai stations and the North and South Nanchang stations, calculated at 85% of the ordinary fare, effective April 1st of this year. Both proposals have been approved by the Ministry of Railways under Order No. 1238. The Ministry has ordered that the one-way joint tickets between the North and South Shanghai stations and the North and South Nanchang stations be temporarily implemented for one year to observe the results.

Deputy Manager of Dairen Steamship Company, Harold Dairen, Passed Away in the United States

The Company Will Hold a Memorial Service

According to news from the local Dairen Steamship Company, the deputy manager of the head office, Harold Dairen, passed away on the afternoon of the 7th at his residence in San Francisco due to a heart condition. Dairen was the son of Robert Dairen, the founder of the company. He served at the Shanghai branch from 1907 to 1925 and was known for his diligence. He was later transferred to the head office in San Francisco and soon promoted to deputy manager. It is reported that the Shanghai branch will hold a memorial service, and friends of Dairen have sent telegrams of condolence.

The Great American Evening Post reports that the local branch of the Dairen Mail Steamship Company received a telegram this morning (the 8th) stating that the company's deputy general manager, Harold Dairen, suddenly suffered a heart attack at noon yesterday at his residence in San Francisco and passed away. According to the report, the deceased was born in 1887 and had come to Shanghai several times between 1907 and 1925. When the American Chamber of Commerce in this city was established in 1915, he was elected as its chairman. He was related to Dairen shipping businesses around the world and also served as the deputy general manager of the Robert Dairen Company and the general manager of the Pacific Steamship Company. The sudden news of his death today has caused regret among his former associates.

Japanese Woman's Tragic Death Case Solved: Murderer is the Woman's Lover, Tanaka Hide, Arrested After the Japanese Police Station's Vigorous Investigation

On the upper floor of the Hongyuan grocery store at No. 279 Miller Road, Hongkou, owned by Ningbo native Chen Hongyuan, lived a Japanese couple named Matsushima Yoshiki. Later, Matsushima moved out due to his work at the Japanese Telegraph Office, which made commuting inconvenient. However, the Matsushima couple had a very close relationship with the Chen couple. When they moved, they introduced a middle-aged Japanese woman to rent the house, agreeing on a monthly rent of 21 yuan in national currency. However, the woman had nothing of value except the clothes on her back. Even the bedding used in the house was taken from what the Matsushima couple had left behind. Since moving in, the woman was never seen doing anything and spent her days wandering the streets. In the evening, people of the opposite sex would come and go. However, the woman had installed an electric bell at the back door of the house and always opened the door herself, so others could not see who she was meeting. Unexpectedly, at noon on the 3rd of last month (March), the Chen Hongyuan couple heard a sound like a raccoon calling from the upper floor. They had not seen the woman for several days and became suspicious. They invited a Japanese neighbor to help them open the door to investigate and discovered that the woman had been dead for many days, in a very horrifying state. They immediately reported to the police station, and the Japanese consulate was notified to conduct a joint examination. It was determined that she had been strangled to death and had had sexual intercourse before her death. However, the identity of the murderer had not been found for a long time, forming a pending case. The details were also reported in this newspaper on March 4th. Now, it is learned that the police station and the Japanese police station spent more than a month investigating and learned that the woman's name was Marumoto Ko, who was a prostitute. The reason for her death was a love triangle. The murderer was one of the woman's lovers, named Tanaka Hide Saburo. He was the one who had met Marumoto Ko at her residence on the afternoon of February 29th. He then colluded with three accomplices to stab her to death with a sharp blade and fled without a trace. The Japanese police station increased its reward to further investigate. Yesterday afternoon, they learned that the main suspect, Tanaka Hide Saburo, was hiding at No. 19 Douhua Lane, Xihua Road. They immediately joined forces with Chinese and Western detectives from the Hongkou Police Station and rushed to the address at around 7 PM and arrested Tanaka Hide Saburo on the spot. He was taken back to the Japanese Police Station and is currently under strict interrogation.

Many Love Affairs at Minhua Elementary School: Female Teacher Sues for Obscenity; Shen Shuqing Accuses Yu Shangxun and Yu Xiangquan; Trial Opened Yesterday, Both Sides Seeking Reconciliation

In January of this year, an interesting lawsuit that caused a sensation in society occurred at Minhua Elementary School, No. 10 Shangwen Lane, No. 251 Weihaiwei Road. The fact was that the school principal, Yu Shangxun (26 years old) from Ningbo, reported to the Chengdu Road Police Station that a teacher, Ding Jiasheng (also known as Ding Hao) from this city, had committed theft, stealing a Western suit worth tens of yuan. Police officers arrested Ding and found several pawn tickets in his suitcase. After reviewing them, one or two items were found to belong to the stolen goods reported by Yu. A public prosecution was filed on the charge of theft. Ding Jiasheng claimed that Principal Yu had stolen his love and deliberately framed him to remove a thorn in his side because he had an affair with a female teacher at the same school, Shen Shuqing (25 years old) from Jiaxing. Now Yu suddenly fell in love with Shen Shuqing, and Shen also transferred her love to Yu, creating a love triangle. The court paid close attention to this issue and summoned Shen Shuqing to court. Shen firmly denied having an affair with Ding and Yu. Ding presented underwear, corsets, and qipaos hidden in her suitcase as evidence. The judge ordered Shen to try them on in court. After the case was published in the newspapers, Minhua Elementary School and Shen Shuqing suddenly sent letters to various newspapers, explaining everything. Shen Shuqing graduated from Jiaxing Women's Normal School, received higher education, and has been a teacher for a long time. She had also been married to someone, and that person was a civil servant in a certain agency in this city. Therefore, at the time, everyone believed that Ding was deliberately insulting her personality. Before long, Shen hired two lawyers and filed a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court, accusing Yu Shangxun and a person named Yu Xiangquan of violating Article 225 of the Criminal Law, "Raping a woman by taking advantage of her mental incapacity or other similar circumstances in which she cannot resist," and Article 229 of the same law, "Using fraudulent means to make a woman mistakenly believe that the person is her spouse and submit to sexual intercourse," for the crime of obscenity. After the court issued summonses, Yu Shangxun's summons was delivered to No. 10 Shangwen Lane, Weihaiwei Road, and signed by Yu himself. Yu Xiangquan's summons could not be delivered because the person was not in Shanghai, so the bailiff returned it to the court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui opened the Eighth Criminal Court and summoned Yu Shangxun. When Yu Shangxun did not appear, the plaintiff's attorney stated that the case was currently in the process of reconciliation, so he requested a ten-day extension for another hearing. Judge Liu then summoned Shen Shuqing to the stand. After inquiring about her age and origin, the plaintiff's attorney again stated that the case was in the process of reconciliation and that there was hope for a peaceful resolution. To avoid exposing the facts of the case to society and the publication of reports, he requested that the facts not be inquired into. If reconciliation was not possible, a decision would be made to inquire again. The court approved the request and declared that if reconciliation was reached, the crime under Article 225 of the Criminal Law could be withdrawn. However, the crime under Article 229 of the Criminal Law could not be withdrawn according to law. The court granted a ten-day postponement, and the case was rescheduled for another hearing at 2:00 PM on April 17th.

Hu San Urinates on Suzhou Creek and Falls into the Water at Xinzha Bridge. On the north bank of Suzhou Creek, there is a dense forest of factories. Often, workers, in a hurry to relieve themselves, would defecate by the river. Yesterday, around noon, a man from Jiangbei named Hu San, currently thirty-six years old, squatted down to defecate at the Suzhou Creek pier. Unfortunately, he was careless and fell backward into the river. Luckily, there were several rice boats docked nearby. The boatmen immediately devised a way to retrieve Hu. They managed to pull him up, but his belly was already greatly swollen, and he was unable to breathe. The boatmen used artificial respiration to expel the water from Hu's abdomen, and he was finally revived.

Shanghai's Ham Sales Industry (Continued)

— Chief Editor of Chinese WeChat

(A General Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce, Part 21)

Northern ham is produced in the Rugao area of Jiangsu, with Rugao having the highest production, followed by Taixing and Jiangdu. Because they are all in Jiangbei, it is called Northern ham. In recent years, the sales of Northern ham have been poor, and production has decreased, even more so than Southern ham. According to investigations, the total production of Northern ham last year was no more than 300,000 pieces, a decrease of 30-40% compared to the previous year. Domestically, Shanghai is the largest market, and internationally, the Philippines is the largest market. Ham is transported from the production area of Rugao to Shanghai in sacks, with 50 pieces per bag, weighing 300 catties. They are first transported by civilian boats or small steamers to Xinsheng Port in Rugao or Tiansheng Port in Nantong, and then transported to Shanghai by Dadat or Datong Shipping Company ships. There are two methods of promotion: one is to have distribution offices in Shanghai (such as Rugao Ham Stores, China Ham Company, Tonghe Tai, Wang Yuchang, etc.), which sell directly; the other is for producers without distribution offices in Shanghai to form joint ventures with Shanghai ham merchants and entrust them with sales, providing a reasonable commission. The ham merchants still existing in Rugao and Taixing counties are listed below:

Yunnan ham is traditionally said to be produced in Tengyue, Yunnan (some say it is produced in Xuanwei, but Shanghai ham merchants all label it as Xuanwei Yunnan Ham). According to people in the industry, Sichuan also produces ham, which is often mixed with Yunnan ham and sold on the market. Yunnan farmers make ham using traditional methods and do not know how to improve them. They simply chop off the pig's ribs along with the breast and do not trim them. Therefore, the ham is large and square, heavy but not beautiful compared to Northern and Southern ham (each piece weighs more than ten catties). However, the meat is tender and more delicious than Jiang ham. But because it contains too much fat (accounting for half of the entire ham), it does not suit the taste of the people in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, so it cannot be sold well in Shanghai. Yunnan ham is mostly transported to Shanghai by Yunnan merchants, mostly stored in wooden boxes, with only ten or so pieces per box. From the place of production to Shanghai, it often passes through Hong Kong, and the freight is quite expensive, so the selling price is also very high. The city's sales are only six or seven hundred pieces a year, which is very limited.

(To be continued)

Letter

To the Esteemed Editor of the Editorial Department:

I am writing to you regarding the news in your newspaper about a strike by workers at our factory due to dissatisfaction with the management. After learning about this, we were extremely surprised. Our factory has been in operation for three years, and the relationship between labor and management has been harmonious. There has never been any dissatisfaction, let alone a strike. On the 6th and 21st of each month, when shifts are changed, the factory is scheduled to shut down for those two days to allow for the repair of machinery. If there is urgent work, the factory does not shut down and double wages are paid. Overtime is also paid according to the law, with their consent, and there are no objections. It is likely that troublemakers are making something out of nothing, intentionally causing chaos. We are deeply concerned that the outside world may not understand the truth, so we are writing this letter to clarify and request a correction. We look forward to your favorable response.

Sincerely,

Wangfu Nail Factory, Binlang Road, West Shanghai

April 8th

To the Esteemed Editor:

After reading your newspaper on the 7th, I was surprised to learn that since the official announcement by the Shanghai Chinese Cotton Cloth Exchange on August 1st of last year to formally auction Japanese yarn, in just over nine months, Japanese yarn such as Rihua Factory's Blue Phoenix, Toyota Factory's Fengnian, Nei Wai Cotton Factory's Shuiyue Caiqiu, Shanghai Factory's Nikko, Qingdao Gongda Factory's Baolai, and Wu Ma, etc., accounted for more than 70-80% of the market transactions, while Chinese merchants only managed to maintain a position in the market with Shenxin Factory's Ren Zhong and a few other brands. Learning from past mistakes, if this continues for some time, I fear that Chinese yarn will be unable to maintain its position. After reviewing your newspaper, I was deeply astonished. The cotton yarn transacted in our market is all Tungi Factory's Golden Rooster standard, and delivery must be made according to our exchange's cotton yarn grade table upon maturity. The cotton yarn currently stored in our warehouse for delivery is all 20-count Hong Kuixing yarn, 20-count Tianguan yarn, 20-count Jincheng yarn, 20-count Da Feiting yarn, 20-count Qiqiu yarn, 20-count Jin Shuangma yarn, 20-count Shuanglu yarn, 20-count Xingshi yarn, 20-count Siji Dafa yarn, 20-count Jinji yarn, 20-count Sanxing yarn, 20-count Zhinv yarn, 20-count Cai Feiji yarn, 20-count Shuang Diqiu yarn, 20-count Jinta yarn, 20-count Muyang yarn, 20-count Qiuhe yarn, 20-count Dan Diqiu yarn, 20-count Cai Kuixing yarn, 20-count Sanyang yarn, 20-count Wufu yarn, 20-count Bao Yarn, 20-count Hongfu yarn, 16-count Shuanglong yarn, 10-count Hong Kuixing yarn, and other Chinese factory cotton yarns, which are obviously present. Your newspaper's report is not only without basis but also contradicts the facts. It is unavoidable to spread rumors. Therefore, I am writing this letter to request an immediate correction to clarify the facts. This is our sincere hope.

Sincerely,

Shanghai Chinese Cotton Cloth Exchange

April 8th

Education News

Ministry of Education Issues Revised High School Mathematics Curriculum Standards (Part 1)

The Ministry of Education has issued revised high school civics curriculum standards, which were reported in yesterday's newspaper. Here are the revised high school mathematics curriculum standards:

First, Objectives: To fully introduce the basic concepts of form and number, to enable students to recognize the relationship between the two, to understand the principles of coherence and consistency in algebra, geometry, and other subjects, and to establish the foundation of general mathematics education; To effectively instill methods of reasoning and proof, so that students can confirm the nature of mathematical methods; To continue to train students' skills in calculation and drawing, making them more perceptive, rich, and agile; To provide students with the necessary mathematical knowledge to study subjects, so as to enrich their ability to examine natural and social phenomena; To ensure that the depth of mathematical principles and the breadth of their applications develop in parallel, so that students can increasingly recognize the value of mathematical principles themselves and the magnitude of their effectiveness, leading to a tendency to continuously strive for improvement; To continue to adhere to the principle of "training can be significantly transferred," paying attention to cultivating students' good psychological habits and attitudes (see Article 5 of the Junior High School Mathematics Standard Objectives), so as to further consolidate them.

Note: Starting from the second academic year, practice exercises can be incorporated into the classroom. For example, solid geometry A, algebra A, and analytic geometry A should each include one hour of exercises in every four hours of class, algebra B should include half an hour of exercises in every three hours of class, and analytic geometry B should include one hour of exercises in every three hours of class.

Third, Curriculum Outline

I. First Academic Year

(1) Trigonometry: 1. Generalized trigonometric functions, basic relationships, radian measure; 2. Variation and tracing of trigonometric functions, graphs; 3. Trigonometric functions of sum and multiple angles, sum and product of trigonometric functions, trigonometric identities; 4. Sides and angles of arbitrary triangles and their areas, trigonometric functions of half angles; 5. Theory and usage of logarithms for solving arbitrary triangles, application problems in surveying and navigation; 6. Inverse trigonometric functions, trigonometric equations; 7. Brief discussion of trigonometric function tables, accuracy of tables. (2) Plane Geometry: 1. Basic principles: A. Purpose and concepts of geometry; B. Geometric axioms; C. Methods of geometric proof; 2. Rectilinear figures: A. Congruent figures and parallel lines; B. Comparison of line segments and angles; C. Concurrent lines and collinear points; D. Symmetrical figures; 3. Circle: A. Relationships between chords, arcs, and angles; B. Properties of chords, tangents, and secants; C. Relative positions of two circles; D. Inscribed figures, circumscribed figures, and concyclic points; 4. Proportion and similar figures: A. Proportional line segments, similarity, and homothety; B. Harmonic range of points and pencil of lines; C. Ceva's theorem and Menelaus' theorem; 5. Area: A. Area of rectilinear figures, proportional line segments and area; B. Geometric calculation problems; C. Measurement of circles; D. Maximum and minimum; 6. Locus: A. Analysis and proof of locus; B. Basic locus and its applications; 7. Construction: A. Basic constructions to basic construction problems; B. Construction methods—locus intersection method, algebraic analysis method, transformation method, and displacement method.

II. Second Academic Year

(1) Solid Geometry (for Group A): 1. Parallel, oblique, and perpendicular relationships between lines and planes in space; 2. Dihedral angles, polyhedral angles; 3. Prisms, pyramids, truncated pyramids, properties of similar polyhedra, regular polyhedra, and their areas and volumes; 4. Properties of cylinders, cones, truncated cones, and their areas and volumes; 5. Intersection and tangency of spherical figures, great circles, small circles, and their poles, spherical angles; 6. Spherical triangles, polar triangles, properties of polygons; 7. Measurement of spherical figures and their areas and volumes; 8. Various application problems concerning polyhedra and solids of revolution. (2) Algebra (for Group A): 1. Basic principles and concepts: A. Laws of operation; B. Summary of number systems; C. Variables, functions, and their limits; 2. Basic rules: A. Basic four arithmetic operations, method of detached coefficients, synthetic division; B. Factoring polynomials using the remainder theorem; C. Using divisibility to find common factors and common multiples; D. Proof of identities, method of undetermined coefficients, method of factoring symmetric expressions; E. Proportion, method of variables; 3. Linear equations and functions: A. Principles of solving equations; B. Linear equations and application problems; C. Graphical solution of linear equations in two variables; D. Simultaneous equations and application problems; E. Integer solutions of indeterminate equations; 4. Inequalities: A. Absolute inequalities; B. Conditional inequalities; 5. Higher-degree equations and rational integral functions: A. Quadratic equations in one variable and application problems, discussion of roots; B. Higher-degree equations; C. Higher-degree equations that can be reduced to quadratic equations; D. Simultaneous higher-degree equations; E. Variation, maximum, and minimum of quadratic functions, graphs; F. Fractional operations, limits of simple indeterminate forms, fractional equations, partial fractions; 6. Irrational functions: A. Extracting roots of polynomials, operations with radicals; B. Irrational equations and application problems; 7. Exponents, logarithms, series: A. Extension of exponents (fractional exponents, negative exponents); B. Properties of logarithms and their applications, brief discussion of table construction methods, accuracy of tables; C. Arithmetic, geometric, and harmonic series and their applications. (3) Algebra (for Group B): 1. Review and supplement of elementary algebra: A. Basic four arithmetic operations, method of detached coefficients, synthetic division; B. Common methods of factoring, method of factoring symmetric expressions; C. Method of undetermined coefficients, partial fractions; D. Various methods of solving equations (especially pay attention to fractional equations, irrational equations, standard quadratic equations, simultaneous quadratic equations, etc.), application problems of various equations; E. Discussion of quadratic equations; F. Extracting roots of polynomials, operations with radicals; G. Properties of logarithms and their applications; H. Proportion, method of variables; I. Arithmetic, geometric, and harmonic series and their applications; 2. Graphical solution of linear and quadratic functions; 3. Inequalities; 4. Binomial theorem (with mathematical induction); 5. Permutations and combinations, brief discussion of probability; 6. Complex numbers; 7. Theory of equations: A. Methods of solving cubic and quartic equations; B. Approximate methods of solving higher-degree equations; 8. Determinants. (To be continued)

Ministry of Education Issues Order on Uniform Sales Methods for Textbooks

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities on the 7th, stating that the pricing of textbooks published by various publishers is not realistic, and outdated textbooks are often sold in remote provinces and counties. Distributors often arbitrarily increase prices and manipulate discounts under the pretext of increasing transportation costs, which has a significant impact on education and requires rectification. The Shanghai Education Bureau was instructed to instruct the Shanghai Book Industry Association to convene a meeting as soon as possible to formulate uniform sales methods for textbooks and submit them for review. The bureau reported that the uniform sales methods for textbooks had been formulated by the Book Industry Association and submitted for review. The ministry reviewed the proposed methods and found them feasible, except for some minor modifications. The order is hereby issued for your information and for distribution to all bookstores under your jurisdiction for compliance.

Attached are the uniform sales methods for textbooks and other books: All books, whether textbooks for large, medium, or small schools, or ordinary new or old books, should be marked with a price; The price of textbooks should be based on the cost of editing and printing, and should be set as low as possible; All books should be sold at the marked price at the door, and no discounts or markups are allowed; For books that have already been published, if the original discount resulted in a higher price, the publisher should immediately review and reduce the price, mark the actual price on the inside cover. In the future, if the price of paper or other reasons require increasing or decreasing the price, the publisher may still make appropriate increases or decreases, but the door must be sold at the final increased or decreased price, without discounts or markups. Price increases or decreases, if textbooks, should be submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval at any time; Books may be sold for pre-sale or special prices, but all should be sold at 70% or more of the marked price; Books may be sold with discounts only in the following cases: A. Wholesale commission for the same industry, determined by the industry association; B. School bookstores or cooperatives at 90% of the marked price; C. Libraries at 90% of the marked price, but only two copies of the same book are allowed, and five copies of dictionaries; D. Shareholders or employees of the publisher at 90% of the marked price, but only one copy of ordinary books is allowed, and two copies of textbooks; E. Authors who purchase their own books at 70% of the marked price. If the copyright is jointly owned, no royalties are given, and the price is 60% of the marked price, limited to 30 copies; Publishers or sellers may not hold low-price sales or give away book coupons in the name of commemoration; Books that are unsalable or damaged may be sold in a special discount section, with no discount limit, but the cover must be stamped with the original price section mark; For books sold outside the publisher's main store, a surcharge for remittance and transportation costs may be added, but not exceeding the actual need; The Ministry of Education orders all publishers and sellers of books nationwide to comply with the above provisions. Violations may be effectively regulated by the local industry association or any member of the same industry who requests the local government.

Review of Textbooks Requires Payment of Review Fee

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities on the 7th, stating that according to Article 4 of the revised regulations for the review of textbooks promulgated by the ministry, textbooks submitted for review should be submitted together with the manuscript and sample copies, and review fees should be paid in proportion to the price of the entire book. The education departments of various provinces submit self-edited or代送edited books by others, requesting review, and often do not pay the review fee or the payment does not meet the regulations. In order to effectively comply with the law, all books submitted for review in the future must comply with the current regulations. The order is hereby issued for compliance, and for distribution to the educational institutions under your jurisdiction for compliance.

Mayor Wu and Director Pan Gave Speeches, Mr. Li Reported on the School's Affairs for the Past 40 Years

The National Jiaotong University in Shanghai celebrated its 40th anniversary yesterday and today. Due to the national crisis, the celebration was simple. The details are as follows:

The ceremony ended around 4 o'clock.

The party ended around 5 o'clock. At 7 o'clock in the evening, the entire faculty and students of the school held a 40th-anniversary celebration in the gymnasium. The program included musical performances, Peking opera excerpts, and the screening of the films "Song of Everlasting Regret" and the dramas "Compromise" and "Sunrise." The performances were wonderful, and the atmosphere was lively. It was a rare event after the Industrial and Iron Exhibition.

School Survey

Overview of Shanghai French School (5)

— Hu Zuyin

6. Family Liaison Methods

The school has been quite effective in implementing methods for connecting with students' families. The liaison method is to use a school-family communication booklet. This booklet is printed in the form of a handbook and is intended for one year of use. The method of application is as follows: Teachers give this booklet to the students every Saturday to take home and ask their parents to read it. After the parents have read the booklet, they return it to the child on Monday to take to school for the teacher to review. When parents read this booklet, they can sign their opinions or raise questions for discussion with the school. If there are no opinions or questions to raise, they sign their name to indicate they have read it. When teachers review this booklet, they can answer the parents' opinions or questions. Teachers can also sign or raise opinions about a certain student in this booklet for discussion with the parents. When new students enroll, their parents must leave a sample signature in this booklet to prevent students from faking signatures in the future.

The various items included in this communication booklet are worth introducing here. The first item in the communication booklet is to ask parents to fill in the student's name, date of birth, parents' names, address, telephone number, etc., for the school to verify. Below is a clear explanation of the school's grading methods for parents' reference. The second item lists the school's general admission rules, including arrival time, cloakroom, lunch arrangements, leave of absence procedures, suspension and expulsion procedures, self-study homework arrangements, etc. Then, a parents-teacher communication guide is attached, hoping that parents will make the most of this communication booklet and often exchange information with the school to jointly seek the welfare of children. The third item lists several school health guidelines, such as the requirement for new students to have a doctor's certificate before enrollment, vaccination methods, isolation dates for infectious diseases, and various school suspension and disinfection methods. The fourth item is to list the children's academic performance in each subject, with each two weeks as a unit. Teachers can fill in the children's academic performance in each subject for two weeks so that parents can understand their children's academic progress in two weeks. On the other hand, there is a blank form regarding the child's behavior, and parents and teachers can record the child's behavior observed in two weeks for each other's reference. Several copies of this academic and behavioral record sheet are listed for use in one semester. The fifth item is to list the child's academic performance and behavior record sheet for one semester, which can replace the end-of-semester report card. The last paragraph is also attached with the principal's comments on the student's academic and behavioral aspects in one semester. The sixth item is to list a comparative table of the child's work status in one academic year, which represents the child's work performance in one academic year on a monthly basis based on performance points using a curve. Parents can see from this curve whether their children's academic performance is improving or declining at a glance. According to the principal's opinion, the school has used this communication booklet for many years and deeply feels that this booklet is of great help to the connection between the family and the school.

Note: The school welcomes people from the education community to visit on weekdays, but they must first contact the Education Supervisor of the French Municipal Council or the school principal.
