Zhengzhong New Scientific Knowledge Book: Giving People a Healthy and Beautiful Baby

This year is Children's Year. In order to meet the actual needs of childcare, the Nanjing Zhengzhong Book Company specially invited Dr. Hu to Nanking to compile the book "Giving You a Healthy and Beautiful Baby" to offer as a knowledge gift for Children's Year. This book is divided into three parts. The first part describes the necessary physiological and hygiene knowledge during pregnancy, the most suitable daily life style, and the preparations for welcoming the baby. It also describes the process before and after childbirth, as well as the matters that should be paid attention to for the mother and newborn after childbirth. Finally, it lists the essentials of breastfeeding, bathing, bowel control, and physical and mental development in the daily life of the baby. In short, from pregnancy to raising a child, everything that is beneficial to the health of the baby is elaborated in detail. It is indeed an essential book for parents to read. It is said that the book is beautifully bound, and many people give it as a wedding gift to newlyweds. Or, during a group wedding, one copy is given to each person, which can be called unique. The Shanghai distribution office of Zhengzhong Book Company on Simalu, Shanghai has already arrived. It is said that each copy is only sold for seven dimes and five cents.

Arrivals yesterday decreased, and local street sales were stagnant. The market seemed to be gradually declining, but suddenly Shantou dealers purchased 340 bags of Shahan brown rice, and inland dealers also purchased 150 bags of Siamese broken rice and rice wine, which kept the market afloat. Prices were similar to the boat market. Local street dealers purchased 300 bags of Wenzhou willow rice and over 1,000 bags of Gan Wan rice, with no significant price differences.

Seafood: New Kelp Still Far Away

Kelp Silk Prices Also Follow the Rise

Kelp: Due to the limited stock in the production area last year and the scarce supply in the Shanghai market, market prices have gradually increased. Currently, the price list is as follows: Tokachi kelp at 9.8 yuan, Nemuro, Hamanaka, Kawaji, Kunashiri, Atsuhishi, etc., at 9.2 yuan, Onishiso at 8.8 yuan, Shucho at 8.4 yuan, Cat Foot at 8 yuan, Select Foot at 7.8 yuan, Second Grade at 7.5 yuan, and Third Grade at 6 yuan. It is said that the goods arrive and are cleared immediately, with few remaining in stock. The new season is still three months away. If customer sales do not stop, the market is likely to continue to rise.

Kelp silk prices have risen due to the increased cost of raw materials, and sales prices have followed suit. High-quality goods in commercial buildings now cost no less than 1.02 yuan. Osaka goods, Double Dragon brand, are priced at 8.5 yuan, and Golden Dragon and Blue Dragon brands are priced at 7.67 yuan, but the goods are coarse and crude, and low quality is unbearable to look at.

Sugar Market: Difficult to Realize the Transformation of Chaoqing Sugar into Coarse White Sugar

Yesterday, the sugar market was stable with a slight increase in customs gold, but transactions were limited and failed to translate into price increases. The association's list price for spot No. 24 coarse granulated sugar was 22 yuan, and for transit sugar, it was 6.95 yuan, with no changes. Dong Chi Bai sugar also lacked fluctuations. Only a few transactions of spot No. 8 Dong Bai sugar were made at 21.6 yuan, and No. 4 sugar was at 21.95 yuan. Ben Mian Bai sugar, recorded by Rao Ji, was at 20.6 yuan. According to records, the Chao sugar list price opened with over 300 bags of ordinary school red sugar at 12.7 yuan to 12.8 yuan, slightly reduced, with no other openings. Although there were rumors that Chaoqing sugar would be transformed into raw materials for coarse granulated white sugar, there was again disagreement yesterday. The transformation into white sugar is still difficult to realize.

The cooperative association's exchange period was again reached yesterday. The total fixed amount was 5,118 bags, and transactions increased slightly at the original price. No. 5 coarse white Guangzhou goods were sold at 21.85 yuan, selling 440 bags. Yangyang goods were sold at 21.65 yuan, selling 30 bags. No. 2 Five Sheep refined white sugar was sold at 21.1 yuan, selling 268 yuan. No. 4 fork was sold at 20.9 yuan, selling 72 bags.

North-South Goods: Low-Grade Candied Dates Temporarily Scarce

Low-grade candied dates have recently seen active purchases from Guangdong dealers, gradually depleting inventories, and prices have slightly tightened. Sales of high-grade goods are sluggish, with little fluctuation. Yesterday, the market price for high-grade Hui Gong bald-headed dates was 28 yuan, with standard surcharges and refunds for both high-grade and low-grade goods. It is said that Lanxi goods will arrive soon, and with the weather turning hot, goods that are soft and prone to deterioration will inevitably see changes in the market.

Miscellaneous Items: Lily Bulb Flakes Continue to Rise by Two Yuan

Since the market price of lily bulb flakes began to rise, sales have been continuous, leading to a supply shortage and extreme tightness. The current market price has risen again by 2 yuan, from 28 yuan to 30 yuan. Market inventories are extremely thin, and there may be a stockout soon. It is also reported that medicinal dealers are purchasing in the production area, and supplies are limited.

Hardware: French Hesa Iron Spot Goods Sold Out

French Hesa iron has recently seen a sudden stockout of spot goods on the market, resulting in buyers being unable to purchase and expressing regret. As a result, the standard price has gradually risen, with the market price reaching 36.5 yuan per case, an increase of over 1 yuan from before.

Paper-Wrapped Iron Opens Higher Again

The opening price for 200-pound paper-wrapped iron rose by another 2 yuan yesterday, selling for 24 yuan per case. Transactions with manufacturers were still limited. Due to few guarantees, customer dealers made few purchases. Spot goods in the hands of dealers are not numerous, and the arrival of new goods is scarce, so the market is quite firm.

Silk and Tea: New Methods for Inspecting Tea Exports This Year

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry has announced new methods for inspecting tea exports this year. The notice states:

"Our country's tea export trade has been declining year after year. Although there are many reasons for this decline, the lack of improvement in tea itself, and even adulteration, is one of the main reasons. For example, green tea is colored with toxic pigments such as San Yu Huang and Yi Ji Huang, which allows countries hostile to us to conduct anti-propaganda everywhere. Excessive moisture content often allows tea to naturally increase in weight and cannot maintain its original quality. Moreover, unsound packaging leads to damage rates of about 10% in foreign markets. Matters like these are fatal blows to China's foreign tea trade.

This bureau is responsible for inspection and must conduct thorough inspections of each batch of export tea. In other words, the main purpose of tea inspection is to improve the credibility of foreign trade and prevent the export of inferior tea and unsound packaging. Therefore, before the new tea season each year, the Ministry of Industry sets the minimum standards for export tea and announces matters that should be promoted and reformed as the criteria for daily inspection, and informs tea merchants to understand our regulations and produce tea conscientiously, so as not to be subject to export bans and other losses. This year's methods for tea inspection consist of three items. In order to enable tea merchants in various places to understand them in advance, the three regulations are written below:

A. Minimum Standards for Export Tea: 1. Green tea: The standard is Pingshui No. 2 Tea No. 7 Pearl Tea. Black tea: The standard is Hunan Juehong. Other teas: The standard is comparable color and palatable taste.

2. Tea moisture content: The standard is that it must not exceed 8.5%. However, this year, in addition to green tea based on the standard, black tea qualifies at 10.5%, and other teas qualify at 12%.

3. Tea ash content: The standard is that it must not exceed 7%. B. Cotton Methods for Colored Tea

1. When merchants report colored tea for inspection, they must fill in the name of the coloring material used in detail. If necessary, they may be ordered to submit the coloring material used for inspection.

2. Tea that is colored too heavily, or has the same or heavier coloring standards, is prohibited from export.

3. It is prohibited to export tea that uses toxic coloring materials containing metals such as lead, copper, arsenic, chromium, barium, etc. (such as the commonly used light yellow, San Yu Huang, Yi Ji Huang, and sand green), and other inorganic or organic toxic coloring materials.

Inner Box Silk Removal Method

The tea box for export tea must meet the following requirements; otherwise, it will be ordered to be repackaged before it can be exported.

1. Four wooden strips must be nailed to each of the four corners and upper and lower edges inside the box, for a total of twelve strips, to increase the supporting force of the tea box.

2. The inside wall of the lead foil must be properly lined with strong and clean paper to completely isolate the tea leaves from the foil.

3. The outside of the box must indicate the type of tea, trademark (general category), number of pieces, gross weight and net weight (new system), harvesting and production period, tea factory number and location.

The above three newly revised regulations will now be briefly explained. (1) The minimum standard for export tea is carefully determined by examining the situation of internal and external supply and demand. We hope that this minimum standard can be raised year by year, so that the quality of tea exported to foreign countries will improve year by year, so as to maintain the reputation of our Chinese tea for its quality and low price. However, in order to prevent the quality of inland tea from improving, the minimum standard for the past few years cannot be actively raised.

(2) The Moisture Content Standard for Tea: The harm of excessive moisture content in tea is that it easily loses its flavor and cannot be stored for a long time. We have already mentioned this. We have formulated this standard with reference to the tea moisture inspection regulations of various countries, and after many years of our own testing. The method of inspecting moisture content was previously done by baking in an oven. From this year onwards, a new Hoffman method will be adopted, and the results of the inspection will be more accurate. We will compile a separate instruction manual for this new method, so that inland tea merchants can also apply it themselves.

(3) Ash content inspection: Inspecting ash content is sufficient to understand the tea leaves that have been colored and adulterated, because the weight of pure tea will never exceed 7% after it is burned into ash. If it exceeds this, there is no doubt that the tea is impure. (To be continued)

Popular Lectures

Wu Jiang Fisherman

— Su Zihan

It is said that in the past, King Ping of Chu ordered Fei Wuji to go to the state of Qin to find a concubine for his son, the crown prince "Jian." This concubine was exceptionally beautiful, and King Ping was so captivated that he took her for himself, and found another concubine for the crown prince Jian.

Fei Wuji was originally the junior tutor of Crown Prince Jian. Because of this, he gained the great favor of King Ping. However, Fei Wuji feared that Crown Prince Jian would kill him after ascending the throne, so he spoke ill of Crown Prince Jian in front of King Ping. King Ping was furious and ordered Fen Yang to go to Chengfu to kill Crown Prince Jian. However, Fen Yang released Crown Prince Jian, who fled to the state of Song.

Crown Prince Jian's senior tutor, Wu She, was a loyal minister. King Ping also arrested him and imprisoned him, ordering him to write letters to his two sons—Wu Shang and Wu Zixu—intending to eradicate the family. Wu Shang came, but Wu Zixu wanted to avenge his father and brother, and also fled to the state of Song to find Crown Prince Jian.

Unfortunately, a civil war broke out in the state of Song, and Crown Prince Jian could not stay there. He went to the state of Zheng with Wu Zixu, where he was treated well. Later, Crown Prince Jian went to the state of Jin. The state of Jin intended to use Crown Prince Jian as an inside agent to destroy the state of Zheng, and then give the state of Zheng to him. Crown Prince Jian was tempted, but Wu Zixu advised him against it, but he would not listen, and returned to the state of Zheng. Unfortunately, the news leaked out, and Duke Ding of Zheng and Zichan devised a plan to capture Crown Prince Jian and kill him. Wu Zixu protected Crown Prince Jian's son, Sheng, and fled from the state of Zheng, day and night, towards the state of Wu.

Wu Zixu protected the grandson Sheng and escaped from the state of Zheng, living like stray dogs and fish that slipped through the net. One day, they arrived at Zhaoguan, not far from the border between Wu and Chu. Wu Zixu thought that once he passed Zhaoguan, he would be saved. But King Ping of Chu had already offered a reward of fifty thousand shi of grain for his capture, and had posters with his likeness everywhere. How could he pass Zhaoguan!

Wu Zixu was extremely frightened and worried. His own life was not important, but the grandson Sheng was the blood of Crown Prince Jian. If anything happened to him, Crown Prince Jian's line would be cut off! What could he do?

Wu Zixu thought and thought, but could not find a solution. He had no choice but to find a place to stay in a remote area inside Zhaoguan. That night, Wu Zixu's beard turned white from worry.

The master of the house, Donggao Gong, was a chivalrous man. Knowing that Wu Zixu was wronged and harboring grievances, he tried his best to help him. He found someone with a similar build to go out of Zhaoguan together with him, to blend in. Fortunately, Wu Zixu's beard had already turned white, and he looked different from the picture. Taking advantage of the guards questioning others, he and grandson Sheng slipped through Zhaoguan.

Once Wu Zixu passed Zhaoguan, he wished he had wings to fly over the territory of Chu, so that he could save his life and take revenge. After walking for a while, he saw a vast expanse of white river in front of him. Once across the river, he would be in the territory of Wu. Wu Zixu was overjoyed.

But just as he was rejoicing, Wu Zixu heard shouts and the sound of horses' hooves behind him! Ah! The pursuers were coming! It turned out that the guards at Zhaoguan had found out soon after Wu Zixu had slipped through. They immediately pursued him. There was a great river in front of him, and pursuers behind him. There was no way to go to heaven, and no door to the earth. Wu Zixu was extremely anxious.

Wu Zixu protected grandson Sheng and ran to the riverbank. Ah! Not far from the opposite bank, wasn't there a fishing boat drifting by, with a long-bearded fisherman standing on the bow? Savior! Savior! Wu Zixu shouted loudly, "Old man, ferry me across! Old man, ferry me across!"

This fisherman was also a chivalrous man, unwilling to make a living in the bustling world. He only fished on this riverbank, living a leisurely life. He had seen Wu Zixu's likeness at Zhaoguan. Although Wu Zixu's beard had turned white, he still recognized him. He also saw that Wu Zixu was carrying a child with a broad forehead and full cheeks on his back, knowing that he was a noble. Because Wu Zixu was wronged and harboring grievances, the fisherman was moved to act chivalrously and wanted to ferry him across. But he saw the banners from afar, and was afraid that if he ferried him across like this, the pursuers would see him. That would be troublesome, so he sang a song:

"The sun and moon shine, yet time has passed,

I agreed to meet you at the reeds."

Wu Zixu heard this and knew what the fisherman meant. He carried grandson Sheng, disregarding the mud under his feet, parted the reeds, and walked to the edge of the river, where he hid, waiting.

Before long, Wu Zixu heard the sound of horses' hooves, and the shouts had reached the riverbank. The fisherman's boat had not yet come over, frightening him and making him anxious. He didn't dare to breathe, and didn't dare to move, for fear that the tips of the reeds would move and be seen by the pursuers.

Wu Zixu heard the pursuers shouting loudly, "Old man, have you seen anyone come here?"

He heard the fisherman answer, "No."

The pursuers shouted again, "Old man, if you lie, we'll make you regret it!"

Wu Zixu heard the sound of horses' hooves and the shouts go along the riverbank to the right, gradually fading away. Only then did he put down the stone in his heart, exhale a long breath, and think to himself, "This old man is really a good person, saving the lives of me and my lord!"

The fisherman sang again outside:

"The sun has set,

My heart is sad.

The moon is late,

Why not ferry me across?

Things are urgent, what shall I do?"

Wu Zixu heard the song and came out of the reeds to the water's edge. The fisherman's boat was indeed docked there. Wu Zixu carried grandson Sheng and jumped onto the fishing boat. The fisherman moved the oar, and the boat left the shore, heading towards the center of the river.

In the vast expanse of the river, this fishing boat was like a leaf. The fisherman only steered the boat, not talking to Wu Zixu, nor looking at Wu Zixu. Wu Zixu's heart was much calmer than when he was on the shore. Sitting in the boat, the fisherman didn't speak, so he didn't speak either. He just stared blankly at the fisherman's arms moving back and forth, rowing the oar.

In just two or three hours, they reached the opposite bank, which was the territory of Wu. Wu Zixu carried grandson Sheng ashore. The fisherman secured the boat and also went ashore. Wu Zixu was about to thank him, but the fisherman said, "General seems hungry, I'll fetch some food."

Wu Zixu saw this and became suspicious, thinking, "The old man left in such a hurry, could it be that he's going to call people to capture me? But if he wanted to capture me, he could have done so on the other bank, where there were also pursuers. Why would he ferry me and my lord across the river? That can't be. But the old man's actions are really suspicious. I'd better hide for a while."

So, Wu Zixu pulled grandson Sheng and hid in the reeds by the river again.

After a while, the fisherman came with wheat rice and fish soup, but couldn't find Wu Zixu on the riverbank, knowing that he was suspicious of him. There was nowhere to hide on the riverbank except for the reeds, so he knew that Wu Zixu must be hiding in the reeds. He sang a song:

"Man in the reeds!

Man in the reeds!

Aren't you a poor scholar?"

Wu Zixu heard that it was still just the fisherman alone, so he led grandson Sheng out. Seeing the fisherman holding food in his hands, he took it with both hands and sat on the riverbank with grandson Sheng to eat.

Wu Zixu was very grateful to the fisherman, so he took off the sword he wore on his waist, handed it to the fisherman with both hands, and said, "Thank you, old man, for saving the lives of me and my lord. I don't have any gold or jewels with me, so I'll give you this sword for self-defense, as a token of my appreciation."

The fisherman did not take the sword, and smiled, "General Wu, I respect you as a hero, and you are wronged and harbor grievances, so I saved you. The King of Chu offered a reward of fifty thousand shi of grain for your capture, but I don't want it. Would I want your sword? General Wu, don't underestimate me!"

Wu Zixu had no choice but to ask, "Please tell me your name, so that I can repay your kindness in the future."

The fisherman did not answer. Wu Zixu had no choice but to bid farewell to the fisherman, and said, "Old man, please don't tell anyone!"

The fisherman bit his lip, stared at Wu Zixu for a long time, and then said, "General Wu, go. I won't reveal it even if I die."

Wu Zixu and grandson Sheng had walked less than twenty steps when they heard the fisherman shout loudly from behind, "What's the point of a great man not being trustworthy? General Wu, rest assured, the state of Chu will never know that you have gone to the state of Wu."

Wu Zixu was shocked. He turned around and saw the fisherman with both hands pointing to the sky, stepping on one side of the boat's gunwale with his foot. With just one step, the boat overturned, covering the fisherman underneath. A rush of water came, washing away the boat and the man. Unconsciously, he looked at the great river, and cried and kowtowed on the ground, saying, "Me and my lord have received great kindness from you, old man. We cannot repay it, but because of my words, you lost your life. Even if I, Wu Zixu, die ten thousand times, I cannot repay you."

After Wu Zixu finished kowtowing, he led grandson Sheng to the state of Wu.

Joseph Lister (1827-1912)

— Zheng Kan

Joseph Lister was a native of West Ham, England. His father was the inventor of the high-magnification microscope. From an early age, his father supervised him strictly, and he learned to use the microscope very early, and understood the necessity of detailed observation and accurate recording.

Lister was a responsible and enthusiastic young man. He didn't make friends easily, but once he got along with someone, he could treat them with sincerity. He admired and thanked his father very much, and vowed to use the tool invented by his father to do something great. He often prayed silently to the microscope, saying, "Friend, I will definitely work hard, please help me succeed! Otherwise, I will not only fail my father, but also fail others."

Under the microscope, he looked at clear water and dirty water, and saw many active little things: some like mosquito larvae, wriggling at both ends, some like tadpoles, swimming everywhere. He was very interested in these little things, and decided to study them thoroughly. He told his father that he wanted to go to medical school to study bacteria. At the age of twenty-five, he received a degree in medicine from the University of London. Because of his excellent grades, William Sharpey, the famous authority on physiology at the time, hired him as his surgical assistant at the hospital of the University College.

At that time, Pasteur had just invented the germ theory, proving that germs came from outside, not from dead matter and air, reminding people to be wary of the invasion of germs. Unfortunately, most surgeons at the time were stubborn and superstitious in the "spontaneous generation theory." Some even closed their eyes and didn't even look at the microscope, blindly guessing that the reason why wounds festered was because the oxygen in the air fermented in the wound. When surgeons went to the ward to perform surgery, they not only didn't wash their hands or disinfect their instruments, but they deliberately chose to wear dirty clothes. Because the ward was too dirty, clean clothes would be stained by it. He said, "Why wash your hands, they'll get dirty when you perform surgery; why disinfect instruments, they're always in contact with poison." Germs were allowed to spread everywhere without people realizing it. Patients infected each other, the wards were filthy, and everything could be a medium for spreading germs. Therefore, even patients with minor injuries who were hospitalized would develop severe poisoning. A kind of "hospital gangrene" was prevalent in the hospital, and nineteen out of ten patients died from this disease.

At that time, the common treatment for wounds was to first use anesthetic to make the patient unconscious, and then use strong medicine to burn off the gangrenous flesh. When the patient woke up, he found that the new wound was even worse than the old wound, and he was always complaining. Often after a few days, a gray membrane appeared around the wound, becoming an incurable disease, and they would die sooner or later. But this kind of treatment could sometimes cure patients. Patients took the risk of being treated, which was better than waiting to die from "hospital gangrene."

As soon as Lister became a surgical assistant, he noticed this cauterizing treatment. He thought, "How can wounds be healed by burning? It must be that the disease-causing roots in the wound have been burned off. What are these disease-causing roots? If I can find them and come up with a foolproof method to eliminate or isolate them, wouldn't this be a great invention to benefit mankind?" So he examined the diseased, rotten flesh under the microscope, and found that there were active microorganisms in it. He assumed that these active things were the disease-causing roots, but because the evidence was insufficient, he dared not draw a conclusion. Not long after, Sharpey introduced Lister to James Syme, one of the most famous surgeons at the time. Syme talked with him and knew that he was a shrewd and resolute young man, so he kept him as a surgical assistant at the Edinburgh Royal Infirmary, giving him all the conveniences for research.

Lister was very compassionate by nature. He worked in the ward and felt very uncomfortable seeing that most of the patients died from "hospital gangrene," so he looked for ways to save them. He had read all kinds of scientific books, but couldn't find any reason. Finally, he read Pasteur's paper and saw the germ theory invented by Pasteur. He was very surprised and delighted, and exclaimed, "I have the answer, there is a way to save hospital gangrene." He had already assumed that wound festering was caused by germs, and with Pasteur's theory and proof, he knew that his assumption was the truth.

But just knowing that there were germs and not finding a way to eliminate them, Lister still couldn't think of a way to deal with them. He racked his brains to think of a way. How to kill the germs in the wound and prevent the invasion of external germs was now his most serious problem. He experimented for several months, all to no avail, and felt very depressed and anxious. He kept asking himself, "Am I just going to be helpless, and not be able to invent a sterilizing drug?"

One morning, his mind was very clear, and he thought calmly, "What's the use of being anxious? Only a calm mind can do research, otherwise even if there is a great truth in front of you, you won't be able to grasp it." He looked up and saw the sky was clear and boundless, and three or five birds were flying freely in the sky. He suddenly felt something, stretched out his neck and looked far away, saying, "The suburbs must be even more spectacular, why don't I go out and play for a day. Maybe I'm too tired, a tired horse can't even compare to a donkey. Maybe if I rest for a day today, I'll be able to invent a sterilizing thing tomorrow." So he immediately prepared to travel to the suburbs.

Although he said that, he still couldn't forget his work. After only half a day of playing, he ran back. When he got home, he saw his gardener cleaning the ditch, pouring carbolic acid into the ditch to eliminate the odor. He suddenly thought of a reason. He thought, "Carbolic acid can eliminate odors, it must be that it can kill the microorganisms that make the water smell bad. Why don't I try using it as an antiseptic to kill germs."

His first experiment with his antiseptic was a great success. Just then, a child was run over by a carriage, and the broken bone had pierced through the skin of his leg and protruded out. Lister wrapped it with cloth soaked in carbolic acid, and properly reattached the broken bone. As a result, the child's leg did not fester or become infected with hospital gangrene, and he soon recovered. This was an unprecedented miracle. Later, he used his antiseptic to cure many people, and hospital gangrene never occurred in the wards he managed. Syme saw Lister's great invention for the medical community, and was very satisfied, so he recommended him to replace himself as a professor of surgery at the University of Edinburgh.

When Lister first used carbolic acid as an antiseptic, his colleagues strongly attacked him, saying that he was "a crow dressed as a peacock." Later, they saw that Lister's method was indeed effective, and they had to use it and admire him. Lister was not satisfied with this, and continued to work hard to study antiseptics. After years of research and improvement, he eventually produced the most perfect antiseptics today, double-declined zinc and declined mercury ointment.

On Pasteur's fiftieth birthday, scientists from all over the world came to Paris to celebrate his birthday, and Lister also went to congratulate him. Pasteur saw Lister and was so happy that he forgot himself. He hugged Lister in the midst of the cheers of the crowd, with tears of emotion in his eyes, his lips murmuring, as if to say, "You and I are one person. My invention is yours, and your invention is mine."

Publishing Industry

A Discussion of Children's Books

— Zhou Hanmei

Chinese children are the most lacking in education, I think that statement is probably not too excessive, right? Children in cities haven't learned to recognize many "human, horse, cow, sheep," but they can rattle off the mahjong tiles of "zhong, fa, bai"; children in the countryside live in muddy ditches all day long, and there is no talk of education at all. This is from a regional perspective; as for the difference between rich and poor? Then the children of poor families have no opportunity to receive education at all, while the children of wealthy families are buried alive in the arms of their parents' doting. Saying that Chinese children are lacking in education is perhaps still giving twelve points of leeway.

Relatively speaking, those who can receive some education are naturally the families of intellectuals. Under the guidance of wise parents, they always want to choose some beneficial children's books for them to read. In my opinion, children's books in the Chinese publishing industry are still built on this kind of family.

How can all Chinese children receive proper education? Although this question is quite closely linked to children's books, it is not within the scope of this article. Now I want to make some criticisms and contributions to the existing children's books.

The times do not allow us to proceed step by step, everything needs to move forward by leaps and bounds, so how can children's books be an exception? If ordinary children's books still talk about fairy tales, the dialogues of Brother Cow and Brother Horse in this extraordinary period, it would be creating a secluded paradise for children in heaven, rather than in the human world of the Republic of China in the present time and place. Therefore, in my opinion, the first principle of compiling modern children's books should be to cater to the psychology and physiology of children, and compile various books for children to read during extraordinary periods. For example, "The Story of Airplanes," "Children During Wartime," "Dad Put on His Military Uniform," etc., are all excellent topics for children's books. We should compile the common sense of wartime into various interesting stories. I believe that in terms of children's interest, it may be much better than the topics of fairies and Sister Moon! You must know that children's curiosity is certainly abundant, but the reality of the story is more important. Do we still think that the story of fairies can win children's cheers more than the planes soaring in the sky? At the same time, some children's books are best linked to toys, such as the method of making airplanes, etc., which will definitely make children feel more interested. Secondly, the local nature should be taken into consideration when compiling children's books. The current children's books and textbooks in elementary schools all suffer from the same problem, that is, the editor lives in the city, and what he sees is everything in the city, so the topics compiled also pertain to the various things in the city. Therefore, the book can still be applied in the city, but the children in the countryside are confused. Given the breadth of China's territory and the great difference in the level of culture, the needs of various places are of course also very different. Therefore, it is of course impossible to compile a children's book that all children across the country can read, understand, and enjoy reading. Therefore, the second principle of compiling children's books should take into account the different local characteristics of various places. Thirdly, there is the issue of price. I think that a big reason why children's books cannot be popularized and why Chinese children lack education is that the price of books is too high. A children's book often costs a dime of silver, which in the families of Chinese children with weak purchasing power, they have to reluctantly give up. Therefore, most of the current children's books are sold in the libraries of elementary schools across the country, and children rarely subscribe directly. This is a very heavy blow to both the Chinese publishing industry and Chinese children. Therefore, I believe that the third principle of publishing children's books is to reduce the price as much as possible and adopt the principle of small profits and quick sales.

This generation of Chinese children is struggling in a difficult fate. We adults who have the duty of educating children should create more benefits for them!

"Reading Problems of Chinese Production Education" (II)

— Baisha

A. Economic View—Regarding production education as education that cultivates economic production.

B. Social View—Regarding production education as a type of education that develops social production.

C. Vocational Education View—Regarding production education as the embodiment of vocational education, or a part of it.

D. Humanistic Education View—Regarding production education as education for training a "productive personality."

E. Labor Education View—Regarding production education as equivalent to labor education, or a part of it.

F. Science Education View—Regarding production education as simply science education.

As for its objectives, summarized, we can obtain three: 1. Understanding the significance of social production; 2. Training in the techniques of social production; 3. Cultivating the personality for social production.

Chapter Four covers the conditions for implementing production education, categorized into internal and external conditions. The former requires resisting international aggression, eliminating feudal forces, stabilizing social order, unifying political authority, solidifying economic construction, and transforming social psychology. The latter requires reforming the education system, cultivating guiding talent, raising implementation funds, and procuring production equipment. If these conditions are not met, production education can be implemented reluctantly, but it will not achieve good results.

Chapter Five covers the principles for implementing production education: 1. It should not be merely reckless action and experimentation, but comprehensive planning. 2. It should not be mere imitation but should adapt to local conditions. 3. It should not focus solely on production results but should also align with educational principles. 4. It should not waste production but must conform to economic principles. 5. Production education should not be implemented away from production; it should be implemented at the production site. 6. Production education should not be theoretical but must be implemented in production activities.

Chapter Six covers the implementation of production education in various regions. First, it describes the implementing agencies. Although various educational institutions have implementations similar to production education, most are rural improvement agencies; primary and secondary schools are mostly attached to labor courses. Next, it describes production education activities, which can generally be divided into agronomy, animal husbandry, and craftsmanship. Then, it describes the implementation methods: social education agencies focus on exhibitions, publicity, and demonstrations; multilevel schools focus on education-related practice and design. As for guiding personnel and implementation funds, one only sees the qualifications are a mixed bag, and the amount of funding varies widely. Therefore, to achieve perfect production education, one must follow the six principles outlined in Chapter Four.

Chapter Seven is the conclusion, first summarizing each chapter and then stating the book's recommendations.

After reading this book, we can gain a clear overview of the theory and implementation of production education, because it melts the theory and practice of production education into one furnace. We can gain an outline of the implementation situation in various places.

At the end of each chapter, there is a brief conclusion, allowing readers to grasp the outline after reading, to understand the essence of the book, and avoid superficial understanding. If readers are limited by time and cannot read the entire book, then reading the conclusion of each chapter and the conclusion of the entire book can obtain its essence.

The meaning of each section in the book, if not written by the author, is annotated with its source. If readers want to know more details, they can browse the original book, avoiding the pain of searching everywhere.

Appendix One is the implementation status of production education in various countries, detailing the recent implementation status in Russia, Germany, Italy, the United States, and Japan, which can not only be used as a reference but also as a lesson. The merit of "stones from other mountains can be used to polish jade" can also fulfill some obligation!

The appendix also has a bibliography of papers and a bibliography of monographs, almost completely searching for papers on the theory and implementation of production education. Those who study production education can view its index and have no need to search for materials everywhere, feeling the pain of lack.

Although the writing of this book came from the hands of various experts, the fluency of the text, the uniformity of the organization, and the clear outline of the materials are all as if from one person's hand, which also shows the value of this book. (End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discussions

Crime and Economic Problems

— Xing An

Facts tell us that the occurrence of criminal cases in society is mostly related to the economy. Especially under the current deformed social organization, economic problems are the main factor causing criminal behavior. Chairman Lin reported in the Kuomintang Memorial Weekly: Upon reviewing the statistical table of recent inmates submitted by the Judicial Yuan, the total number of male and female criminals is 60,745, and the crimes listed can be divided into four categories: The first category is crimes related to robbery, with 31,309 criminals; the second category is assault and injury crimes, with 9,369 criminals; the third category is crimes against public morals and marriage, with 3,572 criminals; the fourth category is opium and morphine crimes, with 7,594 criminals; in addition, there are 2,111 criminals endangering the Republic of China and committing internal rebellion; the rest belong to other various crimes. From this statistical table, we can see that among the 60,000-plus inmates in various provinces, more than 30,000, whose crimes are directly caused by the economy, account for one-half of the total number of criminals. Although the names of the remaining second, third, and fourth categories of crimes may be assault, injury, marriage, or morphine, if we trace the cause of their crimes, they are also indirectly related to economic problems. This is a major issue worthy of our attention!

Human life cannot escape being dominated by the economy, and clothing, food, and shelter are three indispensable necessities of life. Precisely because of this, when a person encounters difficulties in life, in order to satisfy the desire for survival, they often take risks and engage in criminal activities. This is the origin of most criminal events in society. Every day we open the newspaper and see news of theft, robbery, kidnapping, etc., almost without a day passing by. This is still what has been discovered, and there are already so many. The number of cases that have not been investigated is even more imaginable. In recent years, with the collapse of rural areas, the decline of industry and commerce, and the entire economy in extreme panic, the number of crimes committed in society due to the pressure of livelihood is endless. According to Chairman Lin's report, compared with the same statistics in 1931, the number of robbers and pirates in 1931 was more than 2,500, while the number of similar crimes recently is more than 14,500, an increase of about six times. The number of people who violated the regulations for punishing bandits in 1931 was 600, while recently there are more than 5,000, an increase of about eight times. How serious is this phenomenon! This clearly illustrates the increasingly difficult livelihood of the people!

Faced with the fact that the number of criminal cases in China is accelerating, what methods should we use to deal with it? This is a question that must be considered. What the authorities can do is only to implement legal sanctions. However, can today's criminal events be eliminated by punishment? Lao Tzu said: "The more laws are promulgated, the more thieves there are." An effective method is still to find a way out for the hungry! Because this is the only way to relieve the pain of living under oppression. Therefore, passive legal sanctions cannot prevent the occurrence of criminal behavior.

Homecoming

— Lao Xin

—The Story of Sea Navigation—

As usual, when the cargo ship passes through Dali Xu, if Third Master gives the go-ahead to rest for one night, we can all go home together. I don't know why, as soon as the ship enters the canal, my heart starts to itch, as if I can't rest easy until we dock. Old Seven is even crazier. At this time, he's usually like an ant on a hot pot, jumping around with no energy at all.

This time, after unloading the cargo at Dali Xu, it was almost sunset. Everyone was panting and eager and tired. Only after Third Master rolled up his pants and went to a "tiger-fighting" place in the market to smoke opium did we jump back on the boat and start singing our way home. Old Seven was the first to get excited. He taught us:

"Return to the ship before dawn tomorrow, you idiots. A little later means a little more fun!"

Old Gui has always looked down on him, and Old Gui is actually a little afraid of going home—as soon as he gets home, his yellow-faced wife will start nagging, either asking for money or asking if he brought back sangjisheng from Wuzhou. Bring your ancestors for eighteen generations, sangjisheng? He couldn't even bring back a twig.

It was almost dinner time when we reached the entrance of Da Zhen Village. We split up: Old Gui turned left towards the majestic Runan Ancestral Hall, and Old Seven and I walked into the small door on the right hand in hand. Before we had gone far, the children saw us and rushed out laughing. Seventh Sister-in-law is a very strong woman. When Old Seven is not at home, she also farms five acres of land with her nephews. All year round, she works hard "under the sunny sky, getting soaked in the rain". But sometimes she has a very bad temper, loves to scold people, and loves to gossip. The people in our Dafu Lane all say she is a "street scolder".

I patted Old Seven on the shoulder and walked into my own house. My old mother was cooking, and my younger sister and older sister were embroidering. Besides weaving cloth and picking firecrackers to earn some money, they depended on me—but speaking of me, only Heaven knows.

"Hai, you're back?" It seemed unexpected, and she was strangely affectionate. My mother called me from the lower room. I responded as usual. After that, she instructed my sister: "Pour tea for your brother, your brother has worked hard..." In this way, she was busy preparing dinner again.

I was terribly tired, and my knees hurt as if someone had hit them hard. I flopped down on the kang, and my sister interestingly showed me a picture she had drawn from a cigarette pack. At this time, I felt very sad. I casually counted the money left over from Wuzhou in my pocket—two double dimes and seventeen copper cents. I was vaguely thinking, I don't know what I was thinking about...

"Hai, dinner's ready."

I ate mechanically. Suddenly, Seventh Sister-in-law's "street scolder" ghost-like voice came from the front of the street—"You good-for-nothing, I tell you to bring money home to support the family, or we'll all starve to death! You go out for a month and a half, sailing on a boat, and you don't bring a few small coins home. You still have the nerve to come back. If it were me, I would have jumped into the Bai'e pool and died. ... You say you'll wait for the next time, don't wait until your grandson grows up to get rich, no one believes your words! ... Sailing on those cursed boats, you're sure to risk your life, but if you want to make money, you really have to be reincarnated! You good-for-nothing, you cursed wretch, go to hell!"

My mother sighed. My sister's pale face gently lifted up, and her lifeless eyes stared blankly at me. I felt a little dizzy, and I felt as painful as if I had been stabbed with an awl. I couldn't swallow the rice that my mother, sister, and younger sister exchanged for with their blood. I walked to the bed, lay down, and fell into a deep sleep. I heard my sister saying:

"He's too tired, look at him..."

Very fuzzy, I didn't want to listen anymore, my mind was filled with one tragic scene after another, my body was burning, I had many nightmares, and when I woke up, it was not yet dawn, my head was still heavy and throbbing. When I went to the lower room to water and wash my face, I saw through the window that my mother was sitting by the bed, wearing her reading glasses, mending my younger sister's torn shoes. I don't know why, but I walked into my mother's room, my younger sister was still sleeping soundly, but my older sister had already gotten up early to embroider.

"Hai, are you feeling better? You were constantly talking in your sleep last night."

The loving words pierced me like arrows. I took the remaining money from my pocket and put it on my mother's bedside without looking back, and said with difficulty:

"Mom, I'm going!..."

By the time I ran back to the boat, the sun had just risen from the water.

Tongzi

— You Qi

It was past six o'clock, and the sun was still hanging high on the corner of the mountain. The fields on the mountainside were bathed in the evening glow. The neat rows and the strong ears of grain had a peaceful and tranquil demeanor, like a beauty falling asleep!

When we arrived at the new station, we rested at Li's Inn. The inns in this place don't have any names. No, not to mention that it was the border of Guizhou, since we set out on the road, only a very small number of the inns we stayed in in any town were able to have a name. For the porters, they knew it by heart, what places ×'s store was, how many rooms it had, what the price was, and what kind of person the boss was, all clearly engraved in their hearts.

Although the new station was not big, it had two big inns, Li's Inn and Wang's Inn.

Really, on the mountain road, the porters' predictions are admirable. They can calculate how far they can walk that day and where they must rest at night. Other things, like where to have breakfast, where there is a tea pavilion, where the road is easy to walk, and where it is more dangerous, are all like a family letter, all stored in their stomachs.

The morning of departure was on a brisk and gentle day.

At Mentouqing, it was estimated that we had walked half of the day's journey. Good, let's not bring the leftover vegetable scraps into the mountain city. Tonight, no matter what, we'll be able to feed our small, shriveled stomachs something. So, we took out the salted vegetables and a little chili sauce that we had fried in the lunch box. We didn't cherish them as much as we used to, and in the blink of an eye, they were all sent down our throats.

After crossing Chumi Shop, we had a different feeling in our hearts. Thinking that in a few hours we would leave this difficult journey and begin to come into contact with the ancient city, how could we not be pleasantly surprised? New expectations and new explorations will all be displayed before our eyes. Good, let's wait for the facts to unfold! Here, we sang out-of-tune Peking operas, drums, ditties, and ballads. The sedan chair moved slowly, and the passing guests stared at these strange movements with wide eyes.

——Sir, what kind of opera are you singing?

——Nine tunes and eighteen styles, we have them all.

——This is really rare to hear, he smiles unnaturally: We don't have these things in small places!

We admitted that it was not a lie. Growing up in the mountains in their short lives, how could they hear some foreign provincial scraps?

The film "Everlasting Fame," now showing at a certain theater, depicts the story of a great man in the scientific community who devoted his life to inventing medical skills to benefit mankind.

From this story, I thought of gonorrhea. Gonorrhea still does not have an effective treatment to this day. Page 18

In the evening, we saw the city of Tongzi County, built against the mountain, winding like a snake. The gray-black city walls would not be much different from my hometown, I guessed.

After entering the city, we unloaded our luggage at some inn, and after counting the beads of the abacus, the wages due to the porters were handed over to the foreman. Naturally, there were also some rewards. They left without caring about their lives after today.

After dinner, we inventoried all the items and moved to the Yibin Hostel near the center.

After nine o'clock, Old Zhangtou came here with his inseparable crutch, asking to take our long-distance bus to advance to the province in order to reduce his expenses. Tonight, he was a good talker. He told us many stories about Tongzi, and also talked about many unrelated trivial matters. He didn't leave until eleven o'clock.

Get up early tomorrow and take a stroll around the entire city! I have such a private wish.

Odds and Ends of Tokyo

— Lei Shiyu

(2) Grilled Birds, A Ding, Grilled Clams

As soon as dusk falls, some streets suddenly have structures that look like camps, with canvas reflecting a hazy light. When you get closer, a savory smell wafts out, and the entrance is hung with a few strips of cloth with the rough characters "Grilled Birds" written on them. Don't step past it just because it's too cheap. There are good things to taste inside!

On the table is a tin plate or something holding skewers of pig liver, pig stomach, and so-called "grilled birds," sparrows that have been slaughtered cleanly and naked. There is also a bottle of Japanese sake, mustard sauce, soy sauce, or something else.

You can choose what you like to eat. Liver and stomach cost one or two cents (ten cents in Japanese currency equals a dime) per skewer, and a small bird costs three cents or more. The owner inside, sometimes a couple, sometimes just a woman or a man, listens to your instructions and puts the skewers on the blazing charcoal stove, filling the iron bars one by one to grill. While fanning the charcoal fire, they flip the skewers. When they think it's cooked enough, they pick it up and dip it in a soy sauce vat. You can take it and chew on it while standing.

What does it taste like? That depends on each person's taste, but I think that using the money for one visit to a coffee shop to eat this kind of thing for a month is very economical and guarantees a filling effect. It is said that "grilled birds" are famous and characteristic of Japanese food.

But some don't necessarily set up a tent on the street to do business. They can open a stall in their own small house, as long as they also hang a few strips of cloth with the two characters "grilled birds" written on them at the door.

Because I quite like to eat this kind of thing, I know quite a few such places. But I think the best-tasting one is in Dingqiao District, Suwa Town. I can't remember the name, but it's easy to find because his portrait is hanging on his doorway. The portrait is very similar and distinctive. A man in his forties or fifties has such a long Guan Gong beard: thick, shiny black beards, five or six inches long, from the roots of both ears to his chin. According to him, he did business in Taiwan for many years. He often used one or two Chinese words to express his humor.

Because I only "patronized" a few times on the occasion of visiting friends, but his eyes seemed to have a special congenital structure, and the second time he would ask about the previous time.

"A Ding" shops, like his "grilled bird" shops, mostly demarcate the main hall of their own home to do this kind of business. The difference is that the cloth curtain is written in letters, and the food inside has a different flavor. The food is these things: radish, tofu, eggs,... mixed in a pot and cooked. If you like something, she will clamp it up and put it on a plate for you to eat. There is also cheap wine there, whether you drink it or not is up to you. Some even have stools for you to sit on, which is even more comfortable.

When I lived in Kanda District, I found such a comfortable one. And the old woman's house had two daughters, who were very affectionate in their reception. Especially the eldest daughter almost always played the "shamisen" for us to listen to, and sometimes hummed a few tunes.

As for the price of the food: each piece of radish and tofu is about two or three cents, and an egg is five cents. This doesn't seem very proletarian.

"Grilled Clams" are things like mussels, clams, and snails. The method is the same as "grilled birds," but there is no need to flip them because the shell is opened and placed there to fry until it is done. The price is not cheaper than "A Ding." A clam costs about three cents, and mussels and snails cost five, ten, or fifteen cents, depending on the size. But its taste is better than the first two. This, of course, depends on one's own taste.

Storytelling

Cai Xiaofang's Mao Family Story

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Phoenix Hairpin"

The most amorous are often the most foolish. Ill-fated beauties have existed since ancient times. I, Hui Xian, lost my parents in childhood and had no support. I was a lonely adopted daughter in Lu Dou. The engagement with my cousin was originally righteous. The family spent happy times together. Even more joyful was my cousin's deep affection. Murmuring sweet words of tenderness. I only hate that the nun, Bukong, coveted widowhood. I only regret that gentle words of remonstrance deepened the enmity. The Phoenix Hairpin, broken, was not intentional. It stirred up extraordinary misfortune. The manipulation was merely for revenge. The most hateful people in the world are nuns. Slanderous words were used to harm the maidservant. I endured countless hardships and grievances. My aunt's anger did not subside, and her heart changed even more. She actually made me live alone in the temple and suffer bullying. The evil nun once tempted me to a vile profession. I vowed to uphold my chastity. How could my beloved know that he went far away to take the exam? A myriad of sorrows, to whom can I confide? Although my love returned and we were fortunate to meet, it only increased my sadness. The lotus flowers blooming on the same stalk are difficult to achieve. Alas, I, given the task of writing a heartbreaking poem, how can I bear to read it? Alas, my teardrops fall

Page 19

Page 20

Page 21

on my silk collar. Alas, I, thinking back and forth, find it hard to dream. Alas, I, tossing and turning all night, cannot sleep. Alas, I, my haggard face, am afraid to face the mirror. Alas, I, lingering in bed, have truly fallen ill. Alas, our ephemera-like marriage is just a fleeting illusion. Alas, I, suppressing my tears and grief, advise my beloved. Alas, I, frequently remember the Lu family's ancestors. Alas, the Kun string should be continued, I repeatedly urge. Alas, I, revived from near death, am called by my mother-in-law. I cannot attend to her morning and evening. I wish to temporarily ease my worried brow. You must forgive your daughter-in-law for her unfilial name. I sigh that my sinful fate was predetermined in a past life. Why bother blaming others for the torment? I only hope that Heaven knows my heart. The gatherings and separations in life are like duckweed. I willingly close my eyes and go to the netherworld.

Xu Wenbi's Opening

Hangye (1180) 11:15 AM to 12:00 PM

Opening "Filial Son"

Parents love their son like gold. They protect him in every way with utmost diligence. They hold him in their arms at all times. They are anxious and uneasy. They fear their son is too full or hungry. They worry even more about him being too cold or warm. If the child falls ill, they wish they could take his place. It's like a knife cutting through their heart, causing immense pain. Delicious food and fruit are given to the child first. Leftover rice and scraps are swallowed by the parents. Whatever food there is, they always leave some for their child. Whatever clothing there is, it is always given to the child first. Life may have poverty and wealth. The nurturing of children is the same kindness. Since childhood, they have raised you to be an adult. Parents have exhausted all kinds of efforts. In old age, they rely entirely on your support. Meat and fine clothing are provided to nourish your parents. Always be at their side, attending to them diligently. Afraid that you only care for your wife and children. You have little time to care for your elderly parents. How can there be heartless people in the world? I urge you to quickly be filial to your parents. What are you if you are not filial to your parents? Since ancient times, there have been so many filial sons. Let me explain them one by one in detail. Yu Shun's great filial piety moved the heavens. Elephants plowed the fields, and birds weeded. His stubborn parents often wanted to harm him. Kui Kui delivered grain, transforming his parents. Emperor Wen of Han governed the world with benevolence and filial piety. Empress Dowager Bo suffered from illness for three years. He personally tasted the medicine and did not remove his clothes. Morning and evening, he tirelessly comforted his mother. Zeng Shen, a disciple of Confucius, was filial. When guests came to the house, he was at a loss. His mother bit her finger, and his heart ached. He hurriedly carried firewood and rushed back home. He knelt before his mother and asked the reason. In the Zhou Dynasty, Min Sun Zi Qian was filial. In his hemp clothing, he felt cold and lost his grip on the reins. The old father, hearing this, wanted to divorce his stepmother. He knelt on the ground and begged to keep his stepmother. Zilu Zhongyou, a disciple of Confucius, carried rice for his parents for a hundred miles. Later, when he returned in glory after his parents had passed away, he regretted that they could not share it. Tanzi was naturally filial. His parents only thought of drinking deer milk. He wore deerskin clothing and lived among the deer. He was almost hit by an arrow and his life was nearly lost. He did not claim to be old, Lao Laizi. He danced in colorful clothes to entertain his parents. He slept on the ground, imitating children playing. The elderly parents smiled happily. During the Han Dynasty, Dong Yong's family was poor and destitute. He sold himself to bury his father, moving the heavens. He met a fairy under the Huai tree. He weaved silk to redeem himself.

"Desire" - A Film Longed for by Ten Thousand People

Premiering at the Grand Light Cinema on Friday

Marlene Dietrich's passionate and unrestrained nature has long been familiar to movie fans. The production company has also utilized her special personality to continuously produce outstanding works. Her seductive power on the screen has stirred the heartstrings of countless viewers. Paramount's latest production, "Desire," of course, still strives to utilize her talent to the fullest. The plot tells the story of a female thief who is moved by the power of love and inspires the intelligence to change for the better. The entire play uses a string of stolen pearl necklaces and the beginning and end of their love as the main force of the description. Dietrich plays Mettylin, appearing as a female swindler. Her facial makeup and clothing are very suitable, and her demeanor is also very gentle and mysterious. Later, in the process of falling in love with Tom, she played it even more lingering and enthusiastic. Gary Cooper has been famous in the film industry since he starred in films such as "The Wedding Night" and "Sergeant York," and he has recently been hailed as Hollywood's great lover. This time, he and Dietrich collaborated again after "Morocco," playing a pure and passionate young man, Tom, portraying the psychology of a virgin seeking love and comfort. He can carefully portray both the beginning and the end, and he is indeed worthy of being a master of expression. Director Frank Borzage is a romanticist and sentimentalist. His exquisite skills in handling "Desire" are indeed amazing. In addition, Lubitsch's supervision is like icing on the cake. This film is scheduled to premiere at the Grand Light Cinema on Friday and is indeed a good film worth introducing.

"Father and Son Heroes" - An Account

— (Yulin)

Yihua Company's new sound film, directed by Wang Jue Long, starring Wang Yin, Zheng Mengxia, Wei Heling, Wang Juelong, Jiang Xiu, Guan Hongda, Sun Zeyi, and others, "Father and Son Heroes," is a detective drama with an extremely tense story and responsible for improving social customs. Yesterday, during the filming of the "Bandit Den Street" scene, the number of firearms used and the amount of ammunition consumed were enough to create a brand new era in the Chinese film industry. Now, the types and numbers of firearms are made public below, which can also give a glimpse of how magnificent the scene is and how tense the situation is.

(1) Fifteen real pistols, plus two hundred rounds of ammunition, and twenty fake pistols.

(2) Three real submachine guns with three rows of ammunition, and four fake submachine guns.

(3) One machine gun with one row of ammunition.

(4) Five smoke bombs.

(5) Two police vehicles.

"Waves Washing Sand" - A Short Comment

Lianhua's first dialogue sound film, "Waves Washing Sand," uses the latest American-style radio receiver to receive sound, and the sound recorder is the very experienced Kuang Zanjun, so the clarity and brightness of the pronunciation is rare in domestic films.

"Waves Washing Sand" has a grand theme and a new and powerful performance style, which can create a new record in today's film industry.

Jin Yan's heavy performance and excellent acting skills in this film are the greatest success seen in three years, so all movie audiences should not miss this film.

Zhang Zhizhi's performance of a kind of rude and bold spirit in "The Goddess" has won good reviews. "Waves Washing Sand" is another collaboration between him and Wu Yonggang, the director of "The Goddess," and the mutual cooperation is excellent.

"Waves Washing Sand" is a purely artistic work. It is generally expected that the birth of this film will satisfy movie lovers' appreciation.

"Incarnation Girl" - Unofficial History

— Bai Mu

The screenwriter of "Incarnation Girl" is the famous film theorist Huang Jiamo. He not only adopted a brand new theme in this play, but also opened up an extremely novel path in terms of film form and technique.

The director is Fang Peilin. In the past, he was one of the best set designers in the Chinese film industry. Here, he used delicate artistic techniques to handle this mysterious and wonderful drama. Therefore, in any aspect, "Incarnation Girl" has achieved very beautiful results.

Yuan Meiyun is the "Incarnation Girl" in the play. Due to the plot, she transforms into a man and a woman alternately, her whereabouts are erratic and elusive.

Wang Yin plays Yuan Meiyun's lover, but at first, he didn't know that Yuan Meiyun was actually a woman, so many jokes were made.

Zhou Xuan is infatuated with Yuan Meiyun, but later, when she learns Yuan Meiyun's secret, she cries sadly.

Han Langen plays Yuan Meiyun's cousin, whose mouth is more greedy than a cat's, so many jokes are made and it is full of fun.

Among the whole play, the scene where Wang Guilin discovers Yuan Meiyun's secret is the most mysterious and stimulating.

Xu Manli, Qin Tong, Jiang Xiu, Ye Wenqiu, and Zhao Manna also made extremely outstanding contributions.

The photography is by Yao Shiquan. The beauty of the picture and the softness of the light add a lot of power to the drama.

In short, "Incarnation Girl" is a new sensation film, and it will soon be available to everyone on the screen.
